A SURVEY OF THE LAW. CONTAINING DIRECTIONS how to Prosecute and Defend
Personal Actions, usually brought at COMMON LAW. With the Judges Opinions in
Several Cases.

To which is annexed The nature of a Writ of Error, and the general proceedings
thereupon. With a plain Table for the easy finding out of every particular.

BY William Glisson and Anthony Gulston Esquires, Baristers at Law.

Good communicated doubles it self.

-- Vivere nemo
Nunc sine Lite solet, nec sine Lege potest.
London, Printed for Henry Brom, at the Gun in Ivy-Lane, and Thomas Basset in
St. Dunstans Churchyard. 1659.

THE CONTENTS Of the BOOK,
1. Account. 2. Case. 3. Covenant. 4. Detinue. 5. Debt. 6. Ejectment. 7. Quare
Impedit. 8. Replevin. 9. Trespass. 10. Trover, cand.
Wherein is plainly set down and demonstrated.

1. What their several natures are. 2. How many fold. 3. In what court they
most properly lie. 4. Who may best bring them. 5. Against whom. 6. For what
causes. 7. What be Pleas and Bars. 8. What Judgments and Executions.
The Epistle Dedicatory.
TO THE Professors and Practisers Of the COMMON LAW OF ENGLAND.
Candid Reader.
THis Tract in French, was bequeathed to me by an Alliance, William Glisson
Esquire deceased, which I have translated into our own Language for the Common
benefit of all. I am not singular in it, for daily experience manifests the
contrary: neither is it a Novelty for Law Books to appear in this dress.
Antiquity may be plead^d, Sr. Germin Perkins, Stanford, Cromp^on, Lambert, Sr
Henry Finch, Dalton, and diverse others have in former days trodden this path.
My desires are it may not be perused by those who read only to fault, what they
cannot mend, but by those whose judicious Pen will correct the errors as
Cognizances of humane frailty, I wish it successful to all, be he Pleader or
Practiser, and that the Common Law of England may shine forth in these Cloudy,
and ecclipsed days is the prayer of him, who is

A Well-Wisher to the Laws HEN. APPLEGARTH.
Staple-Inne, January 20th. 1658. 9

Common Law By act of Law Guardian in Soccage Next of Kin. A Stranger. Account
is by Bailey of a Court or Hundred in Law in case of a subject. of a Ma^nor
house etc. in deed in case of the king. By his own act. Receiver By other hands
in law in case of a Subject. By his own hands in deed in case of the King.
Statute Law Marlebridge cap. 17. Against a Gardein in Soccage. Marlebridge cap.
23. Against a Bailey vaga^ant. Westminster. 2. cap. 23. For Executors. 2^. Edw. 3.
cap. 5. For Executors of Executors. 3. Edw. 3. cap. ^1. For Administrators. 23.
Hen 8 cap. 8. Collectors for repairing of Goal^ shall account to Justices of
peace. 2. and 3. Mariae cap. 8. Against Head-Constables or Churchwardens. 43.
Eliza. cap. 2. Overseers of the poor shall account to Justices of peace. 1.
Jacobi cap. 9. Against Church wardens and Constables for forfeirures* of

Account against a Guardian in Soccage.
In what Court Account lies against a Gardein in Soccage.
IT lies in the County or Common Ban. Not. br. 117. b.

It lies not before the Shrieve 43 Edw. 3. fol. 21. pl. 11. Thorp; For Brook,
Account 14. says the Shrieve cannot assign Auditors.

A good plea to say the Land is ancient demean, because the reality may come in
question, Coke 5 part, fol. 105. A. Aldens case.

It lies not in the Marshalsey: Coke 10. part, 74. b. Marshalsey.

Who shall have a Writ against Gardein in Soccage.
The Heir in ward shall maintain an Action after the age of fourteen years, or
at his full Age at his election. Littleton.

But Not. br. 118. b. he shall not have it till the age of 21 years. Crook
fol. 131. pl. 106. by reason of the words of Marlebridge cap. 17. scil. (cum ad
aetatem pervenerit) 3 and 4 Mariae. Dyer. 137. pl. 25. New tenures 3. b. 18.
Edw. 3. 55. pl. 76. 29. Edw. 3. fol. 5. pl. 13. Vide Regist. origin. 136. Lib.
Intra 21. D. 8 R. 2. Guard. 166. 10 Rich. 2. Account 132. Doct. Stud. fol. 14.
b. old Not. br. 91. A.

If the heir in such case dye before his full age, his Executor shall maintain
an Action of Account, Crook 131. Pl. 106.

Yet note the heir in Gavel-kinde at fifteen years brought an account against a
Guardian in Soccage, and shows, by the Custom he may alien at such age; and
for this cause he was awarded to account, per Welby. 29 Edw. 3. fol. ^. pl. 13.

The Executor of an Heir shall have an Account: per Westminster. 2. cap. 23.
Littleton 27. A. Crook 131. Pl. 106.

Executor of an Executor shall have an Account by 25 Edw. 3. cap. 23. Com. 290.

Filius and Here Is Domini defuncti non habebit breve de computo, quia pertinet
ad executionem administrationis bonorum defuncti. Regist. Orig. 135. b.

Recusant shall not have an action for any thing that is seized into the hands
of the King. 3. Jac. cap. 5.

Against what person Account lies as Guardian in Soccage.
Account lies against any that takes the profits before the Ward be of the
age of fourteen years. Littleton Na. Br. 118. D. 4 Hen. 7. 6. 10 Hen. 6. 7. 13
Edw. 3. Account 77. 29 Ed. 3. 5. Pl. 13.

But if one occupy, and after Guardian in Soccage recover in right of the
Ward, the party shall not render an account to the Heir, for the Guardian ought
to account for this* 27 Edw. 3. 79. Guard. 22.

The reason is (as it seems) that the Writ does not make mention of the blood.
Regist. origin. 136. b. neither the Count. Lib. intra.

Account lies not against an Executor of a Guardian, Littleton. Nam non jacet
versus executores, quia mere pertinet ad Curam Christianam, cognoscere de
compto reddendo versus executores. Regist. origin. 135. b. 28 Hen. 8. Dyer: 23.
Pl. 145.

But if Executors account, an Action of debt lies for the Arrearages. 2. Hen.
4. 13. Pl. 2.

And if the Testator covenants to account to the Heir and does not, Covenant
lies against his Executor, Regist. origin. 165. b. Not. br. 145. H.

It lies against a Woman, 19. Hen. 6. b. Newton.

It lies against the Husband and Wife: 18. Edw. 3. 55. Pl. 76.

For what things Account lies.
It lies for woods and underwoods sold, for ^ands, Tenements, Meadow, Pasture;
also for Rents and services, perquisits of a Court ad valentiam. Lib. Intra.
21. B. and C.

Marlebridge cap. 17. Respendeant de exitibus per aequalem computationem,
salvis ipsius custodibus rationabilibus misis suis.

For Fines of Copyhold Land granted by one. Trin. 1. Jac. Com. Bane. Shopland.
versus Rider. Rott. 853.

For the issues and profits of the Lands: Littleton.

For the Marriage of the Heir, if he marry before the Age of fourteen years:
Littleton 27. A.

If the marriage be not as great in value as the marriage of the Heir:
Littleton 27. A.

No Account for the presentation of a Church; therefore the Guardian cannot
present thereunto. Not. br. 33. T. 28 Edw. 3. 89. 29. Edw. 3. 5. 8. Edw. 2.
Presentment 10.

But by Daniel Justice Trin. 1 Jac. Com. Ban. Rott. 853. Shopland against
Rider: the Guardian shall present if the Heir be not of the age of discretion.

It lies for writings, 32 Edw. 3. Account. 60.

The Account against a Guardian in Soccage.
The Heir counts that it was ordained by the Common Council the Guardian should
account, etc. and shows the tenure specially, and that the Defendant had the
custody of the Lands, etc. from such a day for 12 years ensuing and has not
accounted for the issues and profits, etc. and that at such a day the heir was
at full Age. Lib. Intra. 21. b. Sect. 1. 2. 29 Ed. 3. 4. Pl. 13. No. Lib.
Intra. 47 E. Sect. 3.

The Writ against a Guardian in Soccage.
Rex, etc. si A. fecerit, etc. tunc summon. etc. B. quod sit coram Justic.
nostris, etc. ostendens quare cum de Comm. Concilio regni nostri provisum sit,
quod custodes terrarum and t^nementorum quae tenentur in Soccagio haeredes
terrarum and tenementorum cum ad aetatem pervenerint, reddant rationabilem
computum suum de exitibus, terris, and tenementis illis provenient. de tempore
quo custodes illi habuerunt, ratione minoris aetatis haeredis praedictae, idem
B. paefato A. rationabilem computum suum de exitibus proveniend. de terris and
tenementis suis in N. quae tenentur in Soccagio, and quorum custodiam idem B.
habuit, dum praedictus A. infra aetatem fuit reddere contradicit, ut dicitur.
Et ideo, etc. This writ is founded per Marlebridg cap. 17. Not. br. 118. A.
Regist. orig. 1^6.

Note this Writ lies against any one that occupies the land during the nonage
of the ward, whether it be the parents of the Heir or not, Regist. origin. 136.
b. for it makes no mention of the blood, but only of taking the profits.

The writ was Receptor denariorum: A good plea to the writ because he was
Guardian in Soccage, for otherwise he would be twice charged: 18. Edw. 4. 3.
Pl. 17.

The Process against a Guardian in Soccage. 1. before appearance. 2. after
appearance.
Coke 3. part 12. A. Herberts Case.

But per Marlebridge cap. 23. A capias was given against a Baily, and per
Westminster. 2. cap. 11. exigend. given against a Servant, Bailey, Chamberlain, or any
other Receiver: Coke 3. parts 12. A. Harberts Case.

And in an account against a Guardian there shall be a Capias 29 Edw. 3. 5. Pl.
13.

But no exigend. because this was given against a Receiver only: 17 Edw. 2.
Process 203. 17 Edw. 3. 59. Pl. 55. Shard.

Capias or distress he shall be committed to the Fleet: 29. Edw. 3. 35. pl. ^3.

If the Account be adjudged, etc. and be not present in Court, a Capias ad
computandum shall issue forth: 1. Edw. 3. 2. pl. 10. 1. Hen. 7. 1. pl. per
Townshend. Lib. Intra. 18. c. Sect. 1, 2, 3.

Judgment quod computet: the Plaintiff dies, his Executors shall have a scire
facias, (...) he come not in upon the garnishment, an exigend. shall issue
forth: 14 Hen. 4. 1.

The Bar by a Guardian in Soccage: 1. To the Action of Account. 2. Before
Auditors.
When he has the Custody till such a day Lib. Intr. 21. cap. Sect. 2.

A good Bar that he expended so much for necessaries for the Plaintiff:
Littleton.

No Bar to say he was next of Kin, for the occupation is the substance,
Littleton. 29 Edw. 3. 5. pl. 13. 22 Edw. 3. 11. pl. 8. 4 Hen. 7. 6. b. 10 Hen.
6. 7. pl. 21. 13 Edw. 3. Account 77.

That he was never Guardian in Soccage a good Bar: Lib. Intra. 21. b. Sect. 1.

The judgment against a Guardian in Soccage, 1. Of Account. 2. To recover the
thing.
The Judgment is, quod computet, and ideo in 11. part 38. A. Metcalfs Case.
Lib. Intr. 19. D. Sect. 1.

The Judgment is, Ideo consideratum est, W. recuperet versus praefatum M. as
much as he is found in arrearages and dampnae occasion implacitationis: Coke
11 part. 40. A.

E^^^ution against a Guardian in Soccage. 1. per Common Law, 2. per Statute Law.
By the Common Law it was but a Levari facias fieri facias: Coke 3. part 12. A.
Herberts Case.

And this only within the year, for if the year passed he was put to his action
of debt.

If the Process were not continued, 33 Hen. 6. 49. pl. 33.

Per Westminster. 2. cap. 45. Scire facias is given after the year.

Per Westminster. Cap. 2. 18. Elegit is given, Coke 3. part. 12. A.

Per Marlebridge Cap. 23. and Westminster. 2. cap. 11. Capias was given in Process
and by consequence, Capias ad satisfaciendum: Coke 3. part. 12. A.

Per Westminster. 2. cap. 11. If an Accountant before Auditors be found in
Arrearages, he shall be by them committed to the next Goal in execution; but
then they ought to commit him forthwith. Coke 8. part. 119. b. Bonhams Case.
27. Hen. 6. 8. Com. 17.

But if an account be before the Plaintiff, he ought not to commit him to
prison, because the statute says, before Auditors. 45. Edw. 3. 14. pl. 13.

Ex part talis.
Westminster. 2. cap. 11. If Au^itors are assigned by the party, which will not allow
to the Guardian his reasonable allowances, and charges him with the thing he
never received* and him commit to prison, he shall have an Ex part talis. Not.
br. 129. F. 4 Hen. 6. 18. A. pl. 3. Regist. origin. 137. b.

The Writ is returnable before the Treasurer and Barons of the Exchequer at a
certain day, and a scire facias is in the Writ, to warn the Plaintiff and also
the Defendant to be there, Not. br. 129. G. H. Regist. orig. 137.

Account against a Bailey, 1. of a Court o^ Hundred. 2. of a Mannor-house, etc.
In what Court it lies against a Bailey.
IN the County Court: Regist. origin. 135. A. Not. br. 117. b.

In London before the Shrieves: Regist. Orig. 135. A and b.

In the five Ports: Regist. origin* 135. A.

In communi Banco: Not. br. 117. b. Regist. origin. 135. B.

But ancient demeasne is a good plea: Coke 5. part. 105. A. Aldens Case.
Because the Account is of the issues and profits of the Manor: 8 H. 6. 34. pl.
36. 2 Edw. 4. 3. pl. 3.

And the reality by presumption may come in debate, Hobart chief Justice, Hill.
11 Jac. Com. Ban. Rott. 254. Cox and Barnsley.

Who shall have an Account against a Bailey 1. of a Court, 2. of a Manor.
If A. make B. his Bailey of his Court or of a Hundred he shall have Account
against him. Not. br. 118. E.

A. having a Bayly-wick makes B. his under-Bayly he shall have Account against
B. 3 Edw. 3. 54. pl. 24.

A. makes B. his Bailey, which makes C. his deputy, A. shall have Account
against B. but not against C. because C. receives this to the use of B. Not.
br. 119. B. 14 Edw. 3. 100. pl. 8.

Not. br. 117. B.

The profits that the Guardian in Soccage takes after the Age of 14 years, the
Heir shall have an Account during his nonage against him as Bailey: but for the
profits taken before such age, he shall have Account as Guardian; but not
before his full age. Not. br. 118. B. because he cannot be Guardian after the
age of 14 years.

Mayor and Aldermen of London grant the Wardship of an Orphan to A. they shall
have an Account against A. at the full age of the Orphan. 8 Rich. 2. guard. 166.

A. devises to his Executors that they shall sell his land, and that his
daughter shall have part of the money, she shall have an Account at Common law.
4 and 5 Mariae Dyer. 151. pl. 5.

A Lunatic shall have an Account against the Committee, when he comes to his
sound memory; for the Committee is but in the nature of a Bailey. 28 Hen. 8.
Dyer. 26. pl. 164. Coke. 4. part. 127. b. Beverleys Case.

Executor shall have an Account. Not. br. 117. C. 3. Edw. 3. 66. 7. Edw. 3.
269. 5. Edw. 3. 141. pl. 7.

But this was by Westminster. 2 Cap. 23.

And if one has Judgment against a Bailey upon an Account, and dies his
executors shall have a scire facias. 14. Hen. 4. 1.

Executor of an executor shall not have an Account. per Westminster. 2. Cap. 23. 7
Edw. 3. 270. pl. 54.

But this was given. per. 25. Edw. 3. Cap. 5. Com. 290.

Filius et haeres domini defuncti non habebit Breve de Computo super Ballivum,
quia pertinet ad executionem administrationis bonorum defuncti. Regist. Orig.
135. b.

The Count against a Bailey, 1. of a Court, or Hundred. 2. of a Manor, etc.
Counts that from such a day to such a day he had the administration de bladis,
fenis, equis, bobus, vaccis, porcis, bidentibus, carucis, ac de omnibus aliis
rebus, etc. et de, etc. ad mercandizandum et proficuum* faciendum, etc. et ad
rationabilem Computum, etc. Lib. Intra. 17. A. sect. 1. vide more Lib. Intra.
17. A. and b. sect. 1. 2. 3. 4. 5. fol. 17. b. and C. sect. 1. 2. 3. 4. 5. 6.

The Plaintiff ought to Count that the Defendant was Bailey of the Mannor-house
and lands, etc. and yet it is not material whether he had the Mannor-house,
etc. for the Receipt charges him. 9 Edw. 3. 356. pl. 38. Stoner. 27 Edw. 3. 29.
pl. 25.

He need not Count the things particulary, because it may be showed before the
Auditors. Crook. 1 Hen. 8. 153. pl. 2.

But the 49. Edw. 3. 13. 14 Hen. 4. 14. says that it is material.

If Account be brought against one that by Custom ought to gather the rents,
the Count must be special. Crook. 21 Hen. 7. 76. pl. 23.

The Count was against one as Bailey of a house and merchandise occupied by
Ioynt-tenants, ex quacunque causa seu contractu. Lib. Intra. 18. A. sect. 6.

The Count was that he was Bailey at the feast of St. Michael, and good, because
it shall be intended th'archangell. Coke. 11. part. 39. A. Metcalfes Case. 20
Hen. 6. 23.

The Count was against a Tenant per Elegit that he had made waste to the Value.
Old. Not. br. 34.

Conusor counts that the Conusee had levied the sum, or that he had levied
part, and tendered the remnant 47 Edw. 3. 11. pl. 9. and fol. 25. pl. 63.

And so of the Assigns of a Conusor. 25 Edw. 3. 53. pl. 17.

The King is not held to Account against one as Bailey, but may aledge generally
in his information, quod i^e ad computand. Domino Regi tenetur, and if it be
against Executors, tempore mortis suae tenebatur. Coke. 11. part. 90.
Devoushers Case.

The process against a Bailey. 1. Before appearance. 2. After appearance.
At the Common Law the Process was but a distress infinite, Coke 3. part 12.
A. Harberts Case.

But by Marlebridg. cap. 23. a capias was given, Coke 3. part. 12. A.

And per Westminster. 2. cap. 11. process of Outlary is given, Coke 3. part. 12. A.
17 Ed. 2. process 203. 17 Edw. 3. 59. pl. 55. Shard, 29 Ed. 3. 5. pl. 13.

But against Tenant by Elegit, is but a Scire facias, 21 Edw. 3. 2. pl. 6. 5
Edw. 3. 159. pl. 20. Regist. judicial. 73. b. Old Not. br. 34.

And if they appear not being summoned judgment shall be given against them, 5
Ed. 3. 159. 21 Edw. 3. 1.

Conusor shall have a Scire facias against the Conusee, Coke 4. part 67. b. 47
Edw. 3. 11. pl. 9. and fol. 25. pl. 63.

So the Assignee of a Conusor, 25. Edw. 3. 53. pl. 17.

If a Bailey come in by Capias or Exigend. he shall be forthwith committed to
the Fleet, 20 Edw. 3. 35. pl. 63.

So if he come in by Distress, and the Account be adjudged, 29 Edw. 3. 35. pl.
63.

But if the Account be adjudged, and he be not present in Court, a Capias ad
computandum shall issue out against him, 1 Edw. 3. 2. pl. 10. 1 Hen. 7. 1. pl.
1. Townsend Lib. Intra 18. c. Sect. 1, 2, 3,

The Bar to a Bailey. 1. To an action of Account. 2. before Auditors.
Account before Auditors.
A good Bar that he did account before Auditors, 25 Edw. 3. 39. pl. 1. 2 Edw.
3. 45. pl. 13. Lib. intra. 17. A. Sect. 1. he shall show the time and the
Auditors.

But in pleading ought to say that the Auditors were assigned by the Plaintiff,
and not by his assent, 29 Edw. 3. 40. pl. 21.

A good Bar that he did account with the Plaintiff, Lib. intr. 18. A. and B.
Sect. 6. 11 Ric. 2. Stath. Account 46. 45 Edw. 3. 14. pl. 13.

But it is no Bar to say he did account with the Plaintiff after that he had
imprisoned him, 22 Edw. 3. 13. pl. 32.

Account per Executors a good Plea that he did account to the Testator and
shows an acquittance, 1 Edw. 3. 2. pl. 10.

Heir Frank-tenant a good Bar, 28 Edw. 3. 90.

An Abbot brought an account against B. as Property.
Bailey of his Predecessor and pleads that he had a Lease of his Predecessor for
three years, and entered after the fine, and found certain things there, this
is a good bar, 16 Edw. 3. 368. pl. 30.

Defendant said that it was debated between the Plaintiff and his wife, and it
was agreed that the wife should have the Land for her maintenance, and leased
to the Defendant rendering rent, this is a good bar 47 Edw. 3. 18. pl. 34.

An account for the delivery of three Tuns of wine; a good bar for the
Defendant to say that the wife was the common Taverner, and that they were Bayl
for the sale thereof, without the assent of him, and that she sold and paid the
Plaintiff without that that they were his Baylies in any other manner, 13 Rich.
2. Account 50.

Defendant pleads a Lease to him of the Manor, a good bar, 49 Edw. 3. 7. pl.
11.

Account of a house and goods: it is no Plea to say he bought the goods of the
Plaintiff, but must say without that, that he was his Bailey for account-render,
49 Edw. 3. 7. pl. 11.

Payment.
Payment by command of the Plaintiff a good bar, Coke 11. part. 38. B. Metcalfs
case, 1 Edw. 5. 42 Edw. 3. 6. Pl. 21* but this is before Auditors, and not in
bar of the Action.

Servant.
The Defendant said that he was servant to the Plaintiff, and he did chase the
cattle out of the field, without that that he was Baily in any other manner;
for the cattle are hurt he shall have an Action of the case, 7 Hen. 4. 14. Pl.
18.

He was his Surveyer, without that that he was his Bailey, 4 Edw. 3. Account 34.

Statute. Merchant.
The Defendant said that the Plaintiff granted by deed, and shows that when he
came to C. he acknowledged a statute Merchant, the account should not be, and
shows likewise that he did it, this is nothing without saying he delivered it
to the Plaintiff, 20 Edw. 3. Account 79.

V ndee.
Account for the delivering of Tyn, etc. the Defendant said that he delivered
this, and took an obligation in the name of the Plaintiff, this is no bar, 28
Hen. 8. Dyer 29* Pl. 193.

Bailey of woods to sell, it is no Plea to say he had not sold them; because
this comes in debate before Auditors, 14 Edw. 3. Account 131.

The plt. after judgment for him quod Comput. dies, his executors shall have a
scire facias. the which being served if he appear not, an exigend shall issue
out against him. 14. Hen. 4. 1.

The Judgment against a Bailey 1 of Acount 2 To Recover the things.
The Judgment is quod Computet et ideo in 11. part. 38. A. Metcalfs case.
Lib. Intra. 19. b. sect. 1. and 20. D. sect. 1.

Quod computet for parcel and Bar for the remnant. Lib. Intra. 22. A. sect.
12.

The Judgment is ideo consideratum est quod as much as he shall be found in
Arrerages et dampna occasion implacitationis, etc. Coke. 11. part. 40. A.
Metcalfs case.

Scire facias against Tenant per Elegit to Account and not appearing upon
garnishment the Judgment was that the plt. shall recover his lands without any
more process upon the cause of the Account, etc. 5 Edw. 3. 159. pl. 20.

Execution against a Bailey 1 per common law 2 per Statute law.
By the common law he shall have but a levari facias, or fieri facias. Coke. 3
part. 12. A. Harberts case. and this within the year only, for if the year
pass, he was put to his action of debt, if the process were not continued. 33
Hen. 6. 49. pl. 33.

Per Westminster. 2. cap. 45. A scire facias is given after the year.

And per Westminster. 2. cap. 18. Elegit is given. Coke. 3. part. 12. A.

And per Marlebridge* cap. 23. and Westminster. 2. cap. 11. Capias is given in
process.

And per consequence a Capias ad satisfaciendum after Judgment. Coke. 3.
part. A. 12.

And by the statute of Westminster. 2. cap. 11. if an Accountant be found in
arrerages before Auditors he shall be Committed by the Auditors to the next
Goal in execution.

But then the Auditors ought to Commit him to prison forth with. Coke. 8.
part. 119. b. Bonhams case. 27 Hen. 6. 8. Com. 1 7.

But if he Account before the plt. he cannot Commit him to prison* 45. Edw. 3.
14.

Ex part Talis by a Bailey.
Per Westminster. 2. cap. 11. if Auditors be assigned by the party which will not
allow to the Accountant reasonable allowances, or charge him with a thing he
never received and Commit him to prison he shall have a writ ex part talis.
Not. br. 129* F. 4 Hen. 6. 18. A. pl. 3. Regist orig. 137 B.

But if Auditors be assigned by the court and they do not allow reasonable
allowances, he shall not have this writ but shall show it to the Court and they
shall make allowances. Not br. 129. F. 3 Edw. 3. 56. pl. 30.

If it be sued in London and Auditors be assigned by the Court which will not
allow etc. there this writ lies. Not. br. 129. F.

But note in Regist. orig. 137. B. is against it.

But if the plt. assign Auditors there then such writ lies Not. br. 129. I.
Regist. orig. 137. B.

The writ shall be returnable before the Treasurer and Barons of the Chequer at
a day certain, and a scire facias in the writ to warn the plt. and deft. to be
there. Nature. br. 129. Regist. orig. 137.

Who shall have an Account against a Receivour.
Husband and wife shall have an Account upon a receipt dum sola fuit. 22 Hen.
6. 39. pl. 10.

Executor shall have an Account, but this is per Westminster. 2. cap. 23. Not. br.
117. C. 3 Ed. 3. 66. 7 Ewd. 3. 209. 5 Edw. 3. 141. pl. 7. 11 Hen. 4. 479.

But one executor shall not have an account against his Companion. 11 Hen. 4.
79. pl. 20.

If one have judgment against a receiver and dies, his executors shall have a
scire facias. 14 Hen. 4. 1.

If two Merchants occupy in Common and one dye his executors shall have an
Account against the other. Not. br. 117. D.

An executor of an executor shall not have an Account, only, the statute of 25
Edw. 3. cap. 5. Com. 190. 17* Edw. 3. 270. pl. 5.

Filius and haeres non habebit breve de Computo versus Receptorem, quia
pertinet ad executionem administrationis bonorum defuncti. Regist. orig. 135. B.

Guardian of a Church against their predecessors. 8 Edw. 4. 6. P. 5.

And per 2. Marlebridg. cap. 8. they shall have an account against a Bailey or
head Constable of an hundred, etc. for amerciaments, or not repayring
high*wayes.

Guardians and Parishioners shall have an account against Constables and
Churchwardens for forfeitures of Ale-house-keepers, in the same manner as for
other things by the common law. 1 Jac. cap. 9.

Two Joynt-tennants of goods, one of them delivers the goods to the other and
to Render Account* one shall have an account against the other. 43 Edw. 3. 21.
12 Hen. 4. 18: Not. br. 118. H.

The shrieve levy money upon a fieri facias and do not deliver it to the plt.
neither brings it into court, the plt. shall have an account against him. 11
Hen. 4. 58. pl. 8. 20 Hen. 6. 24. A. 21 Hen. 6. 5. A.

If one testify, by his deed that he received 20 l. to bestow for me, I shall
have an Account. Hen. 8. Dyer. 20. pl. 118. 11 Hen. 6, 39. pl. 31.

So if one receive money to my use. Not. br. 117. Q. 6 Hen. 4. 7. pl. 33.

So if A. deliver money to B* to deliver to me. Not. br. 117. Q* 13 Hen. 4. pl.
1. Haukeford. Not. br. 138. A.

A. indebted to B. in 200 p. B. prays C. to receive this for him. A. prays ^.
to borrow this to pay B. C. borrows it of D. to pay to B. but pays it not at
the day. A. was bound to D. for repayment. B. shall have an account against C.
for this belongs to B. in so much that C. had his warrant to receive it. Hill.
12. Jac. com. Ban. Harringdon versus Dean.

A. delivers money to B. to deliver to C. and he pays it not, A. shall have an
account against him. Crook 21 Hen. 7. 69. pl. 2. per Frewicke. King.


The King shall have an account, if goods be devised to him, against the
Possessor in whose hand soever they be. Coke 11. part. 90. A. Devoushers Case.
40 Assi. pl. 35.

If one take goods which appertain to the king, claiming them to his own use:
yet the king shall have an account, Coke 11 part. 90. A. 33 Hen. 6. 2. 35 Hen.
6. 27. B. Nottingham: 8 Eliz. Dyer 249. pl. 83.

Two offer to be bound for A. that he shall serve the king truly in such an
office, and they present him to the king and he does not perform his office,
they shall account to the king, though they are not bound, Coke 11 part. 92. B.
Devousheres case. 30 Ed. 3. Rott. 6.

If one be entitled to an action of Account, and be outlawed, the king shall
have an Account for it, 28 Edw. 3. 92. pl. 10.

If one be indebted to the King and dies, the king shall have an account
against his Executors or Ter-tenant, 5 Eliz. Dyer 225. pl. 33.

Against whom Account lies as Receiver.
It lies not against a Prentise, Not. br. 119. D. 7* Hen. 4. 14. 8 Edw. 3. 310.
pl. 26. for there is no writ in the Register against a Prentise, Coke 11. part.
89. B. Devousheres case.

Per 2. Marlebridg cap. 8. Churchwardens shall have an account against a Bailey
or head Constable for amerciaments or highways.

It lies against the husband for receipt of the wife, Not. br. 118. F.

It lies against a Deputy of a Receiver, for he receives this to the use of his
Master, Not. br. 119. B. 4 Edw. 3. 100. pl. 8.

Executor.
It lies not against an Executor, Not. br. 117. C. Littleton. Regist. orig.
135. B. quia mere pertinet ad curam Christianam cognoscere de computo reddendo
versus executores, 48 Edw. 3. 2. 4 Edw. 4. 25.

But if an Executor will account he shall be charged afterward, 2 Hen. 4. 13.
pl. 2. 19 Hen. 6. 5. A. Fortescue.

Note in the case of the king he shall have account against Executors,
Littleton.

It lies not against an infant, Not. br. 118. D. because he has not
discretion to account, per 21 Edw. 3. 8. pl. 21. Regist. orig. 135. A. 26 Edw.
3. 63. he cannot wage his Law.

It lies against a woman or Chaplyn. Not. br. 118. D.

Churchwardens shall have an account against their Predecessors, 8 Edw. 4. 6.
pl. 5.

Two being bound and both of them account, each of them of the whole, quaere if
Account lies against one only, 5 Edw. 3. 141. pl. 8.

It lies not against a parish Priest that has the offerings, for the Clark
holds the vessel in which they are put, Not. br. 119. E. 25 Edw. 3. 46. pl. 32.
vide 11 Rich. 2. Jurisdiction 18.

The king grants the Toll of a Village, and the said Village, and there were
certain Collectors to receive it, the Village shall have a Commission out of
the Chancery of him that receives this Toll, to hear and determine it, and to
hear their Accounts, etc. Not. br. 119. F.

If any takes the goods of the kings debtors which dies, the King shall have an
account against him, Coke 11 part. 93. A.

It lies for the king against a Debtor or his Executors or Tertenents, 5 Eliz.
Dyer 225. pl. 33. Com. 321. Mines.

But if one purchase to him and his wife, and he become indebted to the King,
and dye, his wife shall not be charged, 5 Eliz. Dyer 215. pl. 33. Contra if he
be first in debt, and but a chattle, 5. Assiz. pl. 5.

If one be an accountant to the king, and become indebted to the king, and
afterward sell a Lease for years, the vendee shall not be charged, because it
is but a chattel, Coke 8. part. 171. A.

One in debt to the king purchases lands with the kings money to some friends
in Fee per covin, and yet takes the profits, the king shall have the lands in
execution, 5 Mariae. Dyer 160. pl. 41. 24* Edw. 3. Rott. 4. Coke 11. part. 92.
B. Devousheres case.

For what things Account lies against a Receiver.
A. delivers three tuns of wine to B. to sell, he shall have an account against
him for them, but then he ought to count the receipt of every sum of every
several man, 43 Edw. 3. 21. pl. 11. 46 Edw. 3. 3. pl. 6. 46 Edw. 3. 9. pl. 4.
Hill. 43 Eliz. Com. Ban. Rott. 1707. Tresham against Ford. A, indebted to B.
and C. indebted to B. A. sends money to B. by his servant, which accepts of it
for the debt of C. and not for the debt of A. yet A. shall have an account
against B. because he cannot accept of this in any other manner then the other
tendered it.

If one receive money to my use he shall account for it, Not. br. 117. q. 6
Hen. 4. 7. pl. 33.

So if A. deliver money to B. to deliver to me, Not. 117. g. 13 Hen. 4. pl. 1.
Haukeford, Not. 138. A.

He which ought to pay me an annuity pays this to another to pay me, or if my
Tenant pay it to another to pay me, I shall have an Account against him, 6 Hen.
4. 8. pl. 33.

A. delivers money to B. beyond the sea to be paid in England, he shall account
for it, Not. br. 118. G. 41 Edw. 3. 3.

Money delivered to one upon the performing of a Condition, if the condition be
not performed the money to be redelivered, he shall account, Not. br. 118. G.
41 Edw. 3. 10. 18 Hen. 8. Dyer 22. pl. 135. 11 Hen. 6. 39. pl. 31.

A. leases tithes to B. rendering rent: A. being indebted to C. assigns B. to
pay this. No account lies for this, 5 Edw. 4. 140, 141.

If goods be devised to the King, account King.
lies for them, Coke 11 part. 9. A. Devoushers case.

If one take goods of the crown, and claim them as his own proper goods, yet he
shall account for them, Coke 11. part. 90. A. 33 Hen. 8. 2. 35 Hen. 6. 27. B.
18 Eliz. Dyer 249. pl. 83.

The Account against a Receiver, 1. By other hands. 2. By his own hands.
The Account was that he was a Receiver Lib. intra. 19. C and D. 1, 2, 3. fol.
20. A. Sect. 4.

Account of the Receipt of Moneys by the hands of the wife and a stranger not
good, because they ought to have been several issues, 43 Edw. 3. 33. Pl. 34.

But if the Account be of the delivery by the hands of the wife of the
Plaintiff it had been good, 5 Edw. 3. 146. pl. 6. Count of Baylment by the
hands of a servant of the Plaintiff, Hill. 4 Eliz. Com. Ban. Rott. 1707.
Tresham versus Forde.

And so of the delivery of a stranger and the wife of the Plaintiff, 43 Edw. 3.
33. Pl. 34.

Account that the Defendant sold a thing to A. and recived 20 l. and another to
another and received of him 10 l. this is naught, for the 10 l. and good for
the remainder, 46 Edw. 3. 3. Pl. 6.

Baron and feme count that the Defendant fuit Receiver to the Testator from
such a time to such a time, end received by the hands of B, etc. and did not
account to the Testator neither to the Executrix dum sola fuit, neither to them
after the coverture, Lib. Intra. 20. A. Sect. 4.

Not. br. 118. F.

Bar.
Bar in detinue is a bar in account, per Briau. 2 Rich. 3. 14. Pl. 19. for the
one and the other affirm property.

Coverture.
The Defendant said that the Plaintiff at the time, etc. was under Covert Barn,
and this was good, 6 Edw. 3. 184. Pl. 5. Vide 18 Hen. 6. 3. pl. 3. 2 Hen. 7. 15.

Delivery.
Delivery to another by the command of the Plaintiff Male: but to say that he
was Bailey to deliver to B. of the which he had a deed, this is good; because he
had not confessed it by the account render, 19 Hen. 6. 5. Pl. 10. 26 Hen. 49.
Pl. 7. 30 Hen. 6. 5. Pl. 4. 41 Edw. 3. 31. Pl. 37. Lib. Iutra. 20. A. Sect. 5.

Account against a Carrier who said that goods were delivered to him to deliver
to B. which he had done without that he was Receiver in any other manner, this
is a good bar, Mich. 40. 41 Eliz. Com. Ban. Burrel versus Callice.

So if the plt. deliver to one 20 p. to carry to Lombard to be exchanged, and
he brings a bill of exchange for the money without that that he was a Receiver
for account render, for by this he does not confess the recits for
Account-rendering. 5 Hen. 5. 4. pl. 10. 28 Hen. 6. 9. pl. 1. 3 Hen. 6. 4. pl. 4.

So if the plt. deliver to one 20 p. to obtain a discharge under the great
Seal of Customs 10. Hogsheads of wine, the which he has done this is good. 30
Hen. 6. 5. pl. 4.

Redelivery.
Redelivery to the plt. without accquittance not good. 39 Edw. 3. 19. pl. 21.

So if it be with an accquittanc. 3 Edw. 3. 52. pl. 13. becuse by this he has
confessed the receipt for account-render.

But this is good before Auditors. 29 Edw. 3. 35* pl. 1.

The defendant pleads that he, as messenger of the plaintiff received of C.
being provost to the plaintiff and this paid and delivered to the plaintiff,
this is no bar because by the Receipt he is liable to the account. 6 Edw. 3.
185. pl. 7. 29. Edw. 3. 20. pl. 11.

More.
An account of a Receipt by the hands of B. 1. of May, till the first of July,
it is no plea that B. is dead 3 of May because because he may receive this the
2 of May. 8 Hen. 6. 32. pl. 28.

Obligation.
A. delivers 20 l. to B. to redeliver; B. binds himself to pay this; no bar in
account. 4 Edw. 3. 125. pl. 45.

Payment.
Defendant pleads, the plantif being in his debt commands him to receive of B.
so much to his own use as will satisfy his debt, which he does without that
that he was his Receiver for account-render, and good. Lib. Intra. 20. A. et B.
sect. 6. 5 Edw. 4. 29. B. Brian.

But if he confess the receipt upon account and commands him afterward to
retain the debt, this is no bar. 28 Hen. 6. 7. pl. 9.

Robery.
No plea that he was factor and was Robbed, but a good plea before Auditors.
Coke. 4. part. 84. A. 41 Edw. 3. 3. pl. 9.

Vende.
Vende and takes an obligation no bar. 28 Hen. 8. Dyer. 29. pl. 193.

Unison Receiver.
Upon Recipt by others hands, a good plea that he was never Receiver by their
hands. 10 Edw. 4. 8. A. 7 Edw. 3. 259. pl. 13. 8 Edw. 3. 285. pl. 34. 7 Edw. 3.
242. pl. 1. 24 Edw. 3. 66. pl. 74. 25 Edw. 3. 39. pl. 24.

But 5 Edw. 3. 159. pl. 22. this is not good* but shall say generally, that he
never was his Receiver.

If one testify his receipt by deed he cannot plead that he never was his
receiver. 10 Edw* 3. 383. pl. 18.

Defendant pleads that he is executor of B. and that he received the money as a
debt of B. this not good, because the Plantiff supposes him his receiver; but
ought to say, without that, that he received it as the money of the Plaintiff,
11 Hen. 4. 79. pl. 20. 13 Hen. 4. pl. 1.

Note if the Receipt be by the hands of the Plaintiff the Defendant may wage his
law, 7 Edw. 3. 269 pl. 52.

So upon the delivery of the wife of the Plaintiff, 13 Hen. 4. 8. 43 Edw. 3.
33. pl. 31.

But upon a Receipt by other hands he cannot, 9 Eliz. Dyer 265. pl. 2. 22 Hen.
6. 39. pl. 10. 5 Edw. 3. 159. pl. 22. 33 Hen. 6. 8. B. Moyle. because the
Receipt lies in notice of the Country.

An Executor brought an account upon the delivery of the Testator, the
Defendant cannot wage his law, 7 Edw. 3 269. pl. 52.

Outlary.
Outlary of the Plaintiff after the Receipt a good bar, although he had a
Charter of pardon, 28 Edw. 3. 92. pl. 10.

Accord.
A good plea that after the Receipt he married the daughter of the Plaintiff,
and it was then agreed that he should keep the money, 12 Hen. 4. 18. A.

So that he put the money in a bag, and that he should keep it in liew of a
debt, 28 Hen. 8. 7. pl. 9. Delivery and Redelivery.


Delivery over by command of the Plaintiff a good plea, 19 Hen. 6. 5. pl. 10.
Lib. Intr. 20. A. Sect. 5. 42 Edw. 6. pl. 21.

Redelivery.
Re-delivery good without an acquittance, because he cannot compel the
Plaintiff to make an acquittance, 29 Edw. 3. 35. pl. 1. 6 Edw. 3. 185. pl. 7.
29 Edw. 3. 20. pl. 11. but it seems it may be a good plea before Auditors.

Expenses.
Expenses reasonable shall be allowed to a Factor, 3 Edw. 3, 56. pl. 30.

A Factor pleads that he was robbed, Coke 4. part. 84. A. Southcots case 41
Edw. 3. 3. pl. 9.

So for goods lost by Tempest, 3 Edw. 3. 56. pl. 30. 41 Edw. 3. 3. Pl. 9.

So for goods sold under value by reason of war, 3 Edw. 3. 56. pl. 30.

Receipt in Satisfaction.
Defendant said he received money in full satisfaction of a debt of another,
etc. this was held void, because he did not name that he never was his
Receiver, the which was found before Hill. 43 Eliz. Com. Ban. Rott. 1707.
Treshams case.

Vendee.
Vendee takes an obligation in the name of the Plaintiff, a good plea, 28 Hen.
8. Dyer 29, pl. 193.

But then he ought to show that the obligor was sufficient at that time, 3 Edw.
3. 56. pl. 30.

The judgment against a Receiver, 1. of Account. 2. to recover,
1. The judgment is quod computet, and ideo in miserecordia quia prius inde
non computavit, Coke 11. part. 38. A. Metcalfs case, Lib. Intr. 19. D. sect. 1.

Quod computet for parcel, and bar for the remainder, Lib. Intr. 22. A. Sect. 2.

But if he confess part and traverse the other, no judgment shall be till the
other be tried, 41 Edw. 3. Account 34.

The judgment is, Ideo consideratum quod praedictus W. recuperet versus
praefat. M. so much as is found in Arrerages, and dampna occasion
implacitationis, etc. Coke 11. part. 40. A. Metcalfs case.

The King is not held to account against any as Receiver, but generally, quod
ille ad computum domino Regi reddend. tenetur: and against Executors, quod
tenebantur tempore mortis suae, Coke 11. part. 90. Devoushers case.

In Comitatu.
The Writ against a Receiver.
In Com. Ban.
Rex, etc. pr. A. quod just, etc. reddat B. rationabilem computum suum de
tempore quo fuit Receptor denariorum ipsius B, etc. Regist. orig. 135. and
ibidem B. vide diversa brevia de computo versus Receptorem.

But there is another form of a Writ founded upon the Statute of Marlebridge,
Cap. 23. Not. br. 117. H. Regist. orig. 136. B.

A good plea to the Writ that he was Bailey and not Receiver, for otherwise he
shall be twice charged, 3 Edw. 3. 70. pl. 28. 18 Edw. 4. 3. pl. 17.

A good plea to the Writ that he was Guardian in Soccage, 18. Edw. 4. 3. pl. 17.

The Writ shall be always general, and if the cause be special it shall be in
the County, Not. br. 118. F.

The Defendant pleads the Receipt by deed, and demands judgment of the Writ
without showing it, this is no plea to the Writ; because the Receipt and not the
dead is the cause of Action, 1 Hen. 6. 8. 28 Hen. 8. Dyer 20. pl. 121. But the
9 Edw. 4. 50. B. per Choke contra. 2 Hen. 6. 9. quaere.

No plea to the Writ if they do not agree with the Plaintiff concerning the
manner of the Receipt, 4 Hen. 6. 12. pl. 4.

The Process against a Receiver, 1. before Appearance. 2 after.
At the common law the Process was but a distress infinite, Coke 3. part. 12.
A. Harberts case.

But per Marlebridg cap. 23. a Capias is given, Coke 3. part. 12. A.

And by Westminster. 2. cap. 11. Process of Outlary is given, Coke 3. part. 12. A. 17
Edw. 3. process 203. 17 Edw. 3. 59. pl. 55. Shard. 26 Ed. 3. 5. pl. 13.

A Scire facias shall issue against Tenant per. Elegit to account, 21 Edw. 3.
2. pl. 6. 5 Edw. 3: 159. pl. 20. Regist. Judicial. 73. B. Old Not. br. 34.

And if he come not upon summons returned, Judgment shall be given against
him, 5 Edw. 3. 159. pl. 20. 21 Edw. 3. 1.

Conusor of a Statute shall have a Scire facias against a Conusee de Account,
Coke 4. part. 67. B. 47 Edw. 3. 11. Pl. 9. and fol. 25. Pl. 63.

So the Assignee of a Conusor, 25 Edw. 3. 53. Pl. 17.

But then he cannot surmise that it was appraised and found of base value, 17
Edw. 3. 36. Pl. 6.

If a Receiver come in by a Capias or Exigend, he shall be forthwith committed
to the Fleet, 29 Edw. 35. Pl. 63.

So if he come in by distress, and the account be adjudged against him, 29 Edw.
3. 35. Pl. 63.

But if the account be adjudged against him, and he be not present in Court, a
Capias ad computandum shall issue out, 1 Edw. 3. 2. Pl. 10. 1 Hen. 7. 1. Pl. 1.
Townsend Lib. Intr. 18. Sect. 1, 2, 3

Judgment given quod computet, the Plaintiff dies, the Executors shall have a
Scire facias, which being served, if he appear not an Exigend. shall issue
forth, 14 Hen. 4. 1.

But if the Defendant be taken per Capias ad computandum, and dies in prison, a
Scire facias lies not against his Executors, 10 Edw. 4. 7. 41. Assize.

Bar by a Receiver. 1. to an Action of Account. 2. before Auditors.
Bought.
The Defendant pleads, he bought the goods of the Plaintiff, and he brought
this Action for them, a good Bar, 14 Hen. 4. 19. Pl. 21.

Accord.
The Defendant pleads, that it was agreed that he should be bound to the
Plaintiff for the principal and use, the which he did, this is a good Bar, 22
Hen. 6. 55. Pl. 32. for this drowns the contract: otherwise he ought to plead
this before Auditors.

So if the Plaintiff grant, that if the Defendant pay 20 l. will withdraw his
Action, a good Bar: because by way of Accord, 7 Edw. 3 325. Pl. 11. 18 Edw. 3.
39. Pl. 35.

No plea that he put it in a bag, and that the Plaintiff agreed that he should
keep it in liew of a debt; because the Receipt for account-render is confessed,
28 Hen. 6. 7. Pl. 9.

The Count was that he did account of such a Sum such a day, and year, and
place, before A. and B. Auditors assigned by the Plaintiff, a good Bar, Lib.
Intra. 19. D. Sect. 3. 25 Edw. 3. 39. Pl. 1. 2 Edw. 3. 45. Pl. 13.

Count of diverse sums received between such and such a day, and pleads to
parcel of the time, that he has fully accounted, and to the Remainder that he
was not his Receiver, there he ought to show of what he had accounted, 30 Edw.
3. 1. Pl. 4.

That he accounted to the Plaintiff from three months to three months a good
Bar, 39 Edw. 3. 5. Pl. 22.

A good Bar that he did account 1o April. but then he ought to say, without
that, that he was his Reciever before or after, 21 Edw. 4. 66. Pl. 47 7 Hen. 4.
14. Pl. 17. 45 Edw. 3. 14. Pl. 13. 34 Hen. 6. 44.

Counts that he was Receiver for seven years it is no Bar, that he accounted 1o
Maii Anno 5o without answering for the two other years because he is to answer
for the whole time, as well for the increase as principal, 7 Hen. 6. 5. Pl. 8.

As to 20 s. received 1o Jun. fully accounted for, and to the receipt afterward
or before that he never was Receiver, 27 Hen. 6. 1. Pl. 8.

A good Bar quod 21. Jannarii Anno, etc. to D. in the County of W. he fully
accounted with the Plaintiff, Lib. Intr. 20. B. Sect. 8, 9, 10. 11. Before the
Writ he did account with the Plaintiff, a good Bar, 4 Hen. 6. 43. pl. 4.

But he ought to account to the Plaintiff before he is imprisoned, or else no
Bar, 22 Edw. 3. 3. pl. 32. 7 Hen. 4. 14. 34 Hen. 6. 44. pl. 4.

For the Plaintiff cannot commit him to prison, for Westminster. 2. cap. 11. gives
this only to Auditors, 45 Edw. 3. 14. pl. 13.

Account brought by Executors a good Bar, that they did account to the Testator
and show his acquittances, 1 Edw. 3. 2. pl. 10.

Defendant pleads award by Arbitrators that he redeliver the goods, this is
naught; but if he had been charged only with the safety of them, then good, 2
Hen. 5. 2. pl. 6.

Account upon a Receipt by other hands, Arbitrament is a good Bar, 22 Hen. 6.
39. pl. 10.

Execution against a Receiver, 1. per Common Law. 2. per Statute Law.
1. By the Common Law it was but a Levari facias, or Fieri facias, Coke 3.
part. 12. A. Harberts case.

And this only within the year, for if the year was past, then an Action of
debt.

Unless the Process be continued, 33 Hen. 6. 49. pl. 33.

2. Per Westminster. 2. cap. 45. a Scire facias is giv en after the year, Coke 3.
part. 12. A.

Per Marlebridge cap. 23. and Westminster. 2 cap. 11. a Capias was given in Process,
and by consequence a Capias ad satisfaciendum in execution, Coke 3. part. 12.
A. Lib. Intra. 18. C. Sect. 1, 2, 3.

Per Westminster. 2. cap. 11. if the Accountant before Auditors be found in
Arrereages, he shall be committed by them to the next Goal in execution: the
same law is if he will not account before Auditors, 10 Edw. 3. 387. pl. 28.

But this shall be forthwith, Coke 8. part. 119. B. Bonhams case, 27 Hen. 6. 8.
Com. 17.

But if he account before the Plaintiff he cannot commit him to prison; for the
Statute says before Auditors, 45 Edw. 3. 14. pl.

But the Accountant to the King shall be imprisoned, and his goods and lands in
execution per the Common law, Coke 3. part. 12. B. 5 Eliz. Dyer. 224. Com. 32.

Ex part talis.
Per Westminster. 2. cap. 11. If Auditors be assigned by the party which will not
allow reasonable charges to the Receiver, or charge him with a thing he never
received, and then commit him to prison, he shall have this writ. Not. br. 129.
F. 4 Hen. 6. 18. A. pl. 3. Regist. orig. 137. B.

But if Auditors be assigned by the Court which do not make allowance, yet they
shall not have this Writ, but may complain to the Court, and they shall order
them, Not. br. 129. F. 3 Edw. 3. 56. pl. 30.

If one be sued in London, and the Court assign Auditors and make not
allowance, etc. they shall have this Writ, Not. br. 129. F. but note Regist.
origin. 137. contra.

The Writ shall be returnable before the Treasurer and Barons in the Exchequer
at a certain day, and a scire facias in the Writ to warn the Plaintiff in the
Account, and also the Defendant to be there, Not. br. 129. G. and H. Regist*
orig. 137.

Note that account lies in one Writ against a Bailey and Receiver, Not. br.
116. P. 21 Hen. 6. 21. pl. 42. 9 Edw. 3. 356. pl. 38. and pl. 40. 14 Hen. 4.
20. pl. 25. vide the Writ, Not. 117. C. Regist. orig. 135.

Vide the Count, Lib. Intra. 17. B. Sect. 1.

And for all the other parts they are in the same manner as is described before
in Bailey and Receiver.

1. Quid. 2. Quotuplex.
Action upon the Case.
Action upon the case is either by 1. Doing of wrong to another -- 1.
Inheritance Real 2. Chattels Personal 3. Body 4. Name 5. Suits in Law 2. Not
doing of a thing ought to be done by -- Law to the wrong of Inheritance Real,
Chattels personal Corpse, Suits in Law. Assumpsit touching Inheritance Real,
Chattels personal, Body, Suits in Law. 3. Misdoing 4. Negligence 5. Deceit in
bargains -- With warranty Without warranty 6. Trover and Conversion in Deed
Law, as to persons discontinued, Wasting, Denial to redeliver.

In what Court it lies.
IN Ban. Regis.

In Com. Ban.

It lies not in the Marshalsey, Coke 10. part. 72. A. 76. A. Marshalsey.

For doing of wrong to the damage of another touching a thing hereditary who
shall have it.
Baron and feme*
Baron and feme join upon an assumpsit to the wife dum sola fuit, and good,
Hill. 9 Jac. Ban. Regis. Wolverton and his wife against Day.

Baron and feme join in Trover and coversion upon a deed for an annuity granted
to the wife, for if he survive, he shall have it, Trin. 40. Eliz. Com. Ban.
Russel and Catesby.

Husband had an action sole upon the assumpsit of the wife, and counted of the
assumpsit to him, 27 Hen. 8. 24, and 25.

Commoner.
Commoner shall have it for feeding his common, though he be but a
Coppy-holder, Coke 9. part. 112. B. Mays case.

But then it shall be such feeding by which he loses his Common, or else
cannot have it in that beneficial manner as he ought, Coke 9. part. 231. A.
Maryes case.

Executor.
Executor shall have it for putting him out of his Term by the Lessor, Not.
br. 92. G. Regist. 97. Coke 4. part. 95. A. Slades case.

For money for grain sold, Lib. Intra. 4. B. Sect. 2. the Court there.

Upon an assumpsit to the Testator to marry or pay 20 l. Lib. Intr. 10. B.
Sect. 5.

Upon an assumpsit to save the Testator harmless of an obligation, Lib. Intra.
12. B. Sect. 2.

Feoffee.
If a Nuisance be made, and Feoffment is made, if this continue as a new
Nuisance, the Feoffee shall have an action, Coke 5. part. 101. A. Penruddocks
case.

Heir.
The heir shall have an action for Nuisance made in the time of his Father, if
it be continued, etc. Coke 5. part. 101. A. Penruddocks case.

Joynder.
Two cannot join for calling them false knave and thief, 28 Hen. 8. Dyer. 19.
pl. 112.

Two cannot sue in the Admiralty where one ought to have Action. 5 Mariae.
Dyer. 157. pl. 39.

Lessor.
Lessor shall have it against Tenant at will for voluntary waste, Littleton 15.
A. 14. Hen. 8. 12. Brown. Coke 5. part. 13. B. Salops case. 48 Edw. 3. 25. Dyer
121. pl. 17. 11 Hen. 6. 38.

But not for negligent or permissive waste, Coke 5. Part. 13. B. Salops case.

Tenant in common.
Tenant in common shall have it against the other for breaking a Gutter between
their houses, 2 Hen. 5. 3. pl. 12.

For making a Limepit in his Land which they have in common, by which the water
surrounds his house, 13 Hen. 7. 26.

Tennants in Common join in an action for Nuisance upon their Land Committed*
because this concerns their profit. Mich. 7. Jac. Ban. Regis. Stone against
Dromage.

For Taking of a Meer-stone. 1 Hen. 5. 1. Lib. Intra. 9. C. sect. 1.

2 Against whom this lies.
Administrator.
It lies against an administrator, upon an assumpsit of the Testator. Lib.
Intra. 4. C. sect. 3.

Which Cuts trees without Cause. 18 Edw. 4. 27.

Bailey.
Against a Baylie of a Baylie of goods. 12 Edw. 4. 13.

Baron and feme.
It lies against Baron et feme for not repairing seabanks upon the land of his
wife. 7 Hen. 4. 31.

Trover and Conversion lies against Baron and feme* for the Conversion is a
disloyal act: which his wife may do. Mich. 7. Jac. Ban. Regist. Drapers case.

Carrier.
Trover and Conversion lies not against a Carrier for delivery to his servant,
but an Action upon the case. Pasc. 9. Jac. Ban. Regis. Wornhall et Bradshaw.

Counselor.
A Counselor is retained to purchase land, and discloses the Counsel by which,
etc. 11 Hen. 6. 18.

Upon an assumpsit to pay a bebt. No. Lib. Intra. Assumpsit.
1. B. sect. 1 Coke. 9. part. 86. B. Pinchons case. 1. Coke. 9. part. 94. A.
Banes case.

Churchwardns.
Churchwardens for not repairing a Gutter. which is a Nuisance to my house. Lib.
Intra. 10. D. sect. 1.

Jonder.
I make an assumpsit, Action lies not against 2 only, but if the plantiff shows
that the others are dead then good and sufficient to show that at the request
of them that are alive, and that the others are now dead. Trin. 7. Jac. Ban.
Regis Brereton and his wife, against King and Milner.

Master.
Against a Master upon sale and warranty of the servant. 11 Edw. 4. 6. Tenant
at will.


Against Tennant at will for voluntary wast. Littleton. 15. A. 14 Hen. 8. 12.
Brown. Coke. 5. part. 13. Salops case. Dyer. 121. pl. 17.

But not for permissive or negligent wast. Coke. 5. part 13. B. Salops Case.

Tenant per elegit.
Tennant per elegit which holds over and cuts the trees after money tendered to
him. 21 Edw. 3. 16.

Tenant in common.
Against a Tennant in common by his Companion for breaking his gutter between
their houses. 2 Hen. 5. plea 12.

For making a lime-pit by which his house is damnified. 13. Hen. 7. 26.

Tenant for years.
A. having an ancient light B. erects a house which stops it, and leases it to
C. yet an Action lies not against C. because the Leassee had done no wrong,
and he could not pull it down. Trin. 13. Jacobi Ban. Regis. Bolds Case.

Vicar.
When a man prescribs in an I Will, and the vicar will not suffer him to make a
sepulcher. No. Lib Intra. 8. b. sect. 7.

Shrieve.
Upon a false return. Lib. Intra. 11. A. sect. 1.

Upon returning nichil where he had sufficient. Lib. Intra. 11. C. sect. 2.

For what things this action Lies.
Trees.
Against a Tennant by elegit that holds the lands after his money tendered him
and Cuts the trees. 21 Edw. 3. 16.

So if tennant at will Cuts the trees. Littleton. 15. A. Coke. 8. part. 13. B.
Salops case. 48 Edw. 3. 25.

If a Bailey cuts trees without cause. 18 Edw. 4. 27.

Chapel.
For disturbing of men to come to my chapel with offerings. 19 Rich. 2.
action upon the case. 52.

Way.
Against the owner of the land in which I have a way and he streightens it. 33
Hen. 6. 26. 1 Estreite.


For trenching of it. Lib. intra. 616. C. sect. 1. 2 Trench. 3 Disturb


For any manner of disturbance in my passage or part of my way so that I cannot
pass so commodiously as I did before. 14 Hen. 8. 31. 21 Hen. 7. 35. 22. Hen. 6.
15. 10 Hen. 7. 21.

4 Stopping of it.
If the whole way be stopped by one that is not owner of the soil, it Lies. 22
Hen. 5. 33 Hen. 6. 26. 10 Hen. 7. 21.

So if tertennant and others stop it. 34* Hen. 6. 4. tamen quaere.

For against tertennant that stops all the way an assize of Nuisance does lie
and not this Action. 22 Hen. 6. 14. 3 Eliz. Dyer. 250. pl. 88. 19 Hen. 6. 29.
pl. 49. Paston. 2 Hen. 4. 11. pl. 48. No. Lib. intra. 12. 6. sect. 10.

But if I have it but for years, Case lies. 33 Hen. 6. 26. Not. br. 176. et
184. L. eodem.

If A. stops my way, and leases the land to B. it lies against B. if he do not
open it; but if A. build a house and leases it to B. there B. cannot pull it
down for my way, for this is waste in B. Trin. 13. Jac. Regis. Bolds case* and
Rutlandshiers case.

But the 11 Hen. 4. Action upon the case lies for stopping of a way in gross
only, and an assize of nuisance for a way appendant. 21 Edw. 3. 2. 6. 34 Hen. 6.
4. pl. 11.

But for stoping of a way in my own land trespass vi et armis lies and not
this Action. 31 Edw. 3. Action upon the case 38. 13 Hen. 7. 26.

But for stoping of a high way the defendant shall be punnished in the Leete
and not by this Action unless the party had a special loss. 27 Hen. 8. 26. 5
Edw. 4, 2. b. 7 Hen. 4. 8. 33 Hen. 6. 26. Coke. 5. part. 73. A. Williams case.
21 Hen. 7. 35. Coke. 9. part. 113. Mayrs case.

Slander of my Title.
If A. says that B. has right in my Land for years Action Lies. Coke. 1.
part. 177. Mildmays case. No. Lib. intra. 30. A. sect. 27. but I ought to show
how I am prejudiced.

A. brought an Action upon the case against B. because that he published that
he had the lease of the land of A. and that he intended to sell it and was
hindered, B. said that he had an Indenture as in the Count is mentioned and
traverseth that he forged it, 1 when B. claims a right, though he had none, yet
the Action Lies not, 2 the Count is good because it is that it was against the
knowledge of B. that it was forged. 3 sciens is not traversable. Coke. 4. part.
18. A. case 14.

Lnad.
For stopping a ditch by which my land is surrounded, Not. br. 88. E. 89. M. 39
Hen. 6. 32. 11 Hen. 4. 82. 14 Hen. 8. 31.

For not scouring a Ditch by which my land is over-flowen. Regist. orig. 100. A.

For breaking of a seabanke by which my land is surrounded. Not. br. 86. F. 89.
B. et C. Regist. orig. 95. A.

It lies not for erecting of Cony-burroughs by which I lose the profits of my

Michaelis. 9. Jac. Ban. Rigis. Ward versus Cheshire. The Plaintiff counts that
he is seized in fee of a Kitchen, in parochia sancti Dunstani in London, and
prescribes to have windows in the backside of the Defendant, and his stopping
up of maximam partem, etc. port action and upon not guilty found per quaer. and
moved in arrest of Judgment.

1. He did not show that the kitchen was ancient; but it was resolved, that it
was employed in the prescription; but by Williams this was was not material: but
Crook e contra by the custom of the city it ought to be stopped if not ancient.

2. For that the quantity was not showed, but resolved it need not be, Coke 4.
part. 49. Com. 249. neither show the Parish in which the backside is, sed non
allocatur because the stopping of the light is the material point, and it was
showed where it was: and the Plaintiff had judgment.

Hill 9. Jac. Regis. Hughes and Keme. A. had an ancient house in London, B.
builds a new one which stops the light of A. per Curiam. 1. that a man cannot
by the custom of London erect a new house, where there was not one before, to
stop the lights of the ancient house. 2. Upon an ancient foundation a man may
erect a new house, and stop the ancient lights of his neighbor; for by the
same reason that his neighbor erected his house more high, may the other at
any time erect his, but he cannot enlarge his in breadth or length to stop the
lights of his neighbor, vide 22 Hen. 6. 15.

School.
If I sue a Schoolmaster for erecting a school in the same Town the action
lies not; for it is no nuisance, 11 Hen. 4. 47. pl. 21. 22 Hen. 6. 14. prisott.

Slander of my Title.
If A. says that B. has right in my Land for years Action Lies. Coke. 1.
part. 177. Mildmays case. No. Lib. intra. 30. A. sect. 27. but I ought to show
how I am prejudiced.

A. brought an Action upon the case against B. because that he published that
he had the lease of the land of A. and that he intended to sell it and was
hindered, B. said that he had an Indenture as in the Count is mentioned and
traverseth that he forged it, 1 when B. claims a right, though he had none, yet
the Action Lies not, 2 the Count is good because it is that it was against the
knowledge of B. that it was forged. 3 sciens is not traversable. Coke. 4. part.
18. A. case 14.

Trade.
1. If one has the trade of a Bakehouse by prescription for the whole Town,

The Writ
Ought to be certain as the Count, except the place and time, 22 Hen. 7. 91.

Prisott.

The Writ shall not be vi and armis, Not. br* 92. E.

former may be alleged vi and armis, Coke 9. part. 50. B. Salops case.

The Process. 1. Before appearance. 2. After.

The Judgment.
For not repairing of a Bank per quod, etc. the judgment shall be to recover

Goods not delivered.
The executor comes to the heir 31 days after the death of the Testator and
demands the goods that are in the house, and he refuses to deliver them, 1 this
is a Convenient time, 2 this wrong is punishable. Mich. 7. Jac. Ban. Regis.
Steedmans case.

Wood and estovers.
1. A. sold 20. cords of wood to B. to have by assignement, and afterward sold
4000. to C. to have at his election, and assigns to B. which he shall cut and
C. takes them, B. shall have an Action. Coke. 5. part. 24. Palmers case.

2. Tenant for years shall have estovers in the wood of B. which shall be cut,
or have an Action, Coke. 9. part. 112. B. Mayers case.

Carrier.
1. Against a Carrier that breaks Pots and glasses, 2 Hen. 7. 2.

lies against the Master, Pash. 9. Jac. Ban. Regis. Wornhall et Bradshaw.

A Horse*
1. For delivering a horse to B. for safeguard, who delivers him to C. to the

9.

2. Against a Smith that pricks my horse. Not. br. 94. D. vide the writ there,

orig. 106. A. 48 Edw. 3. 6. pl. 11.

And if the Smith lends the horse to another who pricks him, Action lies
against the second, 12 Edw. 4. 13.

A servant brought a horse to the smith who pricked him by which the service of
the Master is neglected, the Master shall have an Action. Hill. Jac. Ban. Regis.

Note Actio quod metus causa fuit datur ei qui probabli metu rem suam tradidit,
vendidit vel promisit, versus eum qui metum intulit, et dicitur metus
probabilis qui in virum constantem cadere possit, et non in hominem
metriculosum, Bracton. Lib. 3. cap. 4. fol. 103. B.

Articles.
If one exhibit Articles to a Justice of peace against B. to have him bound to
his good behavior, no Action lies for this because it is in Course of Justice,

acquitted, for it is so employed, 2. ought to have Counted quod inde acquietatus
fuit, or words that do amount to so much, Mich. 7. Jac. Ban. Regis. Rott. 407.
Bell. versus Gamble.

Against a surgeon that impairs the body by his Medicine, 21 Hen. 6. 55. 11

For doing a thing to the damage of another touching his name which is Slander.

Slander
Dicitur quod scandalosum est, generale verbum. that one does to the overthrow
of another; therefore it is conceived that if the words are spoken to the wrong
of another, an Action lies, Kitchen. 173.

Fit autum injuria non solum cum qui^ puguo percussus fuit, verberatus,
vulneratus, vel fustibus cesus, verum cum ^i conviti^m dictum fuit, vel de eo
factum crimen famosum, and hujusmodi. Bracton. Lib. 3. fol. 155. A.

There are 2 kinds of defamations, Spiritual, and Temporal. Not. br. 55.

Note when words are spoken adjectively if they touch one in his Profession or
Trade they are actionable, otherwise not, Coke 4. part. 19. case 15.

Also if they imply or presume an illoyall act then an action lies although
they are spoken adjectivly but if they imply an intention only then an action
lies not. Coke. 4. part. 19. B. case. 15.

Adulterer.
It lies not for calling one adulterer because it belongs to the spiritual
Court, 27 Hen. 8. 17. Coke. 4. part. 17. case 11. but now it does because
Adultry is made death.

Bunkrupt
1. For calling a man Bankrupt it lies not, unless a man be a Merchant or use a
Trade. pash. 40 Eliz. Beckard and Constable. it was there doubted, then one
case was Cited in Ban. Regis. that it did not lie.

2. For saying that B. will be a Bankrupt within 2 days it lies, 6 Edw. 6.
Dyer. 72. pl. 6. Coke. 4. part. fol. 19.

3. A. shows that he was a Shoemaker, and did use to buy and sell per 10 years,
the defendant said that he was a bankrupt, and this was good although he did
not show that he was a shoemaker, for it is employed in that he said he used to
buy and sell per 10 years, Mich. 9. Jac. Ban. Regis. Dayet. Chandler.

4. For calling a Merchant Bankrupt Knave it lies because it touches him in
his profession, Coke. 4. part. 19. A. and. B.

Basterd.
1. For Calling one Basterd if he be an Heir, No. Lib. Intr. 28. sect. 25.
Trin. 25 Eliz. Ban. Regis.

2. A. intends to present B. to a Church and C. says that he is a bastard by
which he is not presented, B. shall have an Action. Coke. 4. part. 17. case. 11.

Bawd.
For Calling one Bawd it lies not, 27 Hen. 8. kitchen. 173. because it belongs
to the spiritual Court.

Bribery.
A. said to B. your Attorney is a bribing knave, Action lies because it
touches him in his profession, Mich. 11. Jac. Com. Ban. Yardly et E^ill.

A. said of an Attorney, You are well known to be a Corrupt man and to deal
Corruptly, Action lies, Coke. 4. part. 16. case. 6.

Barecter.
For Calling a man Common Misseasor or Barector it lies not, Kitchen. 173. A.
vide. 22. Assiz 43.

Cosener.
1. For Calling a man Cousener it lies not, Coke. 4. part. 15. B.

2. Thou art a Cosening knave and have Cosened my 2 Kinsmen of Land worth 6000
l. and I will bring thee to stand upon the Pillory for it, the action lies not,
Kitchen. 173. B.

3. A. is a Cosening knave and I have proved him a Cosening knave for selling
me a saphir for a diamond, it lies not, Kitchen. 174. A.

4. If Sr. John S. may have his will, he would kill all true subjects and the
King, and he is a maintainer of Papists and rebellious persons, upon not guilty
the Jury found, that he said I think in my Conscience ut supra, etc. 1 the
words are Actionable, for scandalum dicitur quod parit ruinam vel occasionem
ruinae, 2 the Jury found the substance and no variance, Mich. 14. Jac. Regis.
Sydenham et May.

Thou art an enemy to the state of this Realm an action lies, Hill. 40. Eliz.
Com. Ban. Hooknell et Smith.

Slander in writing.
It lies for writing a Libell in a paper and affixing it to the Church door by
which I am to enter, 17 Edw. 4. 3. Lib. Intra. 13. B. sect. 4.

False Justice.
For calling one false Justice of peace it lies. 4 Edw. 6. 22.

False Knave. False sure.
It lies not for Calling a man false knave, Kitchen. 173. B.

1. It lies not for suing a man for forgery. 11 Eliz. Dyer. 245.

Because for false action sequiter nulla poena. 2 Rich. 3. 9.

For this is in course of Justice, Coke. 4. part. 14* B.

2. But if one be sued in the star chamber for a thing not examinable, there an
action lies* Coke. 4. part. 14. B. case. 3. No. Lib. Intra. 23. B. sect. 21.

3. But if one appeal in Com. Ban. it lies not, because this is in the nature
of a loyal suit.

Felon.
1. For calling a Judge a Felon, 30. Assize. 19. Kitchen. 173. A.

Forger.
It lies for saying that one had forged a deed, 11 Eliz. Dyer. 285.

Heretic.
1. For calling one Heretic it lies not, because it properly belongs to the
Spiritual Court, 27 Hen. 4. 17. Regist. org. 54. Coke. 5. part. 57. B.
Specotts case.

2. But if one said of a divine that he is a Heretic by which he loses his
benifice or presentation, action lies, Coke. 4. part. 17. case. 11.

Thief.
1. For calling one thief an action lies. 27 Hen. 8. 14. Eliz. Dyer. 236. pl.
26. Lib. intr. 12. D. sect. 2. Hill. 4 Eliz. Com. Ban. Reques case. Dyer. 9.
pl. 112.

Common voice and fame is not sufficient to call a man Thief 26 Hen. 8. 9.
Dyer. 236. pl. 26.

But he may Justify that the plantiff stole sheep, Mich. 13. Jac. Com. Ban.
Cuddinston et Wilkins.

For calling one thief and causing him to be indicted where he was acquitted, 27
Hen. 8. 11 Lib. intra. 12. D. sect. 2.

For saying that A. had stole sheep, 27 Hen. 8. 22.

For saying that A. stole sheep of B. 26 Hen. 8. 9. pl. 11.

A. is a false knave and was at my house on the sessions day at night and would
have Robbed me and did break my doors and did put me in Jeopardy of my life. 28
Hen. 8. Dyer. pl. 171.

A. is infected with such a Robbery that he does smell of it, 14 Eliz. Dyer
317. pl. 8. 6 Edw. 6. Dyer. 72. pl. 6.

There is a nest of thieves at B. and C. is the maintainer of them, and is a
strong thief, Dyer. 75. pl. 2.

Men cannot have their Cattle go up and down the Common but B. and his children
will kill them with Barbors dog, no action lies, Dyer. 118. pl. 79.

Thou art a steal-gown and the first gown that thou did wear thou stollest,
and then did walk up and down in thy stolen gown, and had no gown
until thou did steal one. action lies, No. Lib. intra. 22. D. sect. 20.

Thou art a Thief for thou stollest my sons goods, action lies without averring
that he had goods, Pash. 38 Eliz. Com. Ban. Elin. et Moore.

My master B. has Robbed me of all my goods, action lies without averring that
he was his servant, for that is assets certain, Mich. 15. Jac. Ban. Regis.
Brown et Low.

B. burned my barn, (innuendo) a barn of Corn, action lies not, for it is not
showed a barn with Corn, nor that it was parcel of the Mansion house, and the
innuendo, cannot aid it, Coke. 4. part. 20. case. 16. No Lib. Intra. 24. D.
sect. 22.

A. has stolen my wood, action lies, for wood cannot be intended trees
growing, Pash. 38 Eliz. Com. Ban.

A. does or will prepare to Robb me, action lies, for this tends to the ruin
of A. Mich. 14. Regis. Sydenham et May.

A. Calls B. Thief, and Justifies that he stole sheep, B. pleads the general
pardon after the words spoken, the action lies, for by the pardon the word
Thief is taken away, Mich. 13. Jac. Com. Ban. Cuddingtons case. and Wilkens.

Thou did set on me on the high way, and did take away from me my purse,
and I will be sworn to it, action lies, Pash. 9. Jac. Ban. Regis. Stoner et
holland.

Leper.
1. For Calling one Leper or Leprous knave, Action lies, Intr. Tailor et Baggs.

For leprosus extra communionem positus peter's non potest, Bracton. Lib. 2.
fol. 12. A.

Murderer.
1. For calling one Murderer, Action lies, 6 Eliz. Dyer. 236. pl. 26.

2. Thou have killed my wife, no Action lies, because it appears to the Court
that she is alive, Coke. 4. part. 16. A.

3. Thou did poison thy husband Action lies, and yet it was objected, 1 that
she ought to show that he was dead, 2 that he dyed within the year, 3 that it
was voluntary, Mich. 15. Jac. Ban. Regis. Gardiners case.

4. Thou did poison S. and it shall Cost me a 100 l. but I will hang thee
for it, Action lies, No. Lib. Intra. 25. C. sect. 23.

5. A. said that C. gave counsel to B. to kill me, It lies not because a man
is not punishable without an Action done, Coke. 4. part. 16. Case. 10.

Perjured.
1. For calling one perjured, 2 Hen. 8. 22. Kitchen. 173.

2. But for saying that he had forsworn himself, It lies not, Coke. 4. part.
15. A et B.

Unless he had said in such a Court of Record, Coke. 4. part. 15. B.

3. A. has gotten a Manor by swearing and forswearing, Action lies not
because it is found general, Coke. 4. part. 15. A et B. No. Lib. Intra. 21. B.
sect. 18.

4. W. is forsworn and perjured in swearing at the Common Plea bar, upon the
deed which he then had in his hand, this shall not be intended that he swore
upon the deed but upon the book, ergo the action lies, Hill. 35. Eliz. Ban.
Regis. Rott. 56. Crow.

H. is a perjured old knave in the Court of T. Action lies, for perjuring in a
Court, Baron is punishable, per 5 Eliz. for the right comes in debate there, et
perjurium est ius alienum pervertere, Pash. 40 Eliz. Com. Ban. Hatchman et
Southcotte.

A. says to B. thou have an old Creeple whore to thy mother, for which words
he sued him in the spiritual Court, and produced W. for witness, A. takes
exception to him because he was perjured at the Assizes at D. in such a cause,
W. for this brought his Action against A. which Justifies as aforesaid, 1 this
was a legal course, ergo the action lies not, 2 the Eclesiasticall court may
punish perjury, therefore it lies not, Trin. 15. Jac. Ban. Regis. Westover
versus Dabener.

Thou art perjured and I will pro^e it, Action lies, N. Lib. intra. 26. A.
sect. 24.

For saying that A. was detected of perjury in Starchamber, it lies not because
an honest man may be detected but not convicted, Coke. 4. part. 16. case. 8.

Plague.
1. For saying of an In^holder that he had buried diverse of the Plague that
dyed in his house in his garden, Action lies, Regist. orig. 173. B.

Pox.
M. is a whore and has the Pox, and they have made such holes in her that you
may turn your finger in them, and K. the Srugeon has given her a diet drink
to heal them, take heed how you drink with her, Action lies: 1 for calling her
whore and this is the cause of the Pox, 2. the cure is published, to wit the
surgeon and the drink, 3. the contagion, take heed how you drink with her. ergo
it shall be intended the french Pox, Trin. 15. Jac. Ban. Regis. Milner and his
wife against Reeve.

Profession
1. A. said of B. being a Barrester that he had as much law as a Jack an Apes,
action lies because it is an unreasonable creature not having any law, and it
scandals him in his profession, Mich. 36. et 37 Eliz. Ban. Regis. Palmers case.

Revealer of a cause.
For saying of a counselor he will deceave you, he was of my counsel and
reavealed my Cause, No. Lib. Intra. 22. B. sect. 19.

Rogue.
For calling a man Rogue it lies not, Kitchen. 173. B.

Sedition.
A. says of a Preacher thou have made a seditious Sermon to day and moved the
people to it, Action lies because he is scandalized in his profession, Coke 4.
part. 19. case. 15.

An Action de scandalis magnatum was brought for saying you like of those that
maintain sedition against the Queens proceedings, Coke. 4. part. 12. B.
Cromwells case.

Sorcery.
L. said E. did report that your wife sacrificed her child to the devil to
make away my mother, Action lies, because sorcery is felony, per 11. Jac.
Regis. and there is an evil intention and an act joined together, Pash. 15.
Jac. Lock versus Lock. Traitor.


It lies for calling one Traitor, 27 Hen. 8. 14. 30. Assize. 29. Coke. 10.
part. 130. B. Osburns case.

Thou did speak treason, action lies, 9. Jac. Brereford et Preston.

Walter said P. did say that Mr. Lewis. did say there was no Prince in England,
action lies, and it cannot be intended but Prince Charles, and because it
touches the plaintiff in his Allegiance it shall be taken in the favourablest
sense, as is Fama, fides, occulus non patiuntur Ludum, Hill. 14. Jac. Ban.
Regis. Lewis et Walter.

Userer.
For calling one Userer it lies not, because it merely belongs to the
spiritual Court. 27 Hen. 8. 17.

Whore.
It lies not for calling one whore, Mich. 9. Jac. Ban. Regis. Hudsons case.
Coke. 4. part. 18. A. but it does by the late action.

But in London by customs it did lie before, but if it be removed to Westminster. no
Procedendo shall be granted, for such customs to maintain actions for brabling
words is against the Law. Coke. 4. part. 18. A. case. 13.

For saying of a Maid that she had a Bastard, an action lies, 1 because it is
punishable by our Law, 2 if she be to be married it hinders her preferment,
Coke. 4. part. 16. case. 11. Davies et Gardener.

For doing of wrong to the damage of another, touching suits in Law.

Execution.
1. A. having goods of B. in his house the Sheriff comes and takes the goods in

Admission.
A Coppie-holder by Custom may nominate him which shall succeed him, and name
one, and pray to be admitted, and offer reasonable fine to the Lord which
refuses; the Coppieholder shall not have an action of the Case against the
Lord, because before admittance he had no right, Pash. 13 Jac. Ban. Regis.
Forde and Hoskins.

Bedell of a Hundred.
A Bedle of a Hundred brought his action against many, and prescribes to have

show what estate. 2. it is good against many because all in common are
accessory, 19 Rich. 2. Action upon the Case 51.
