Debt was brought against the father for the Father.
sons commons in a College in Oxon although the father had delivered it to the
Tutor of the son, Pasch. 9. Jac. Ban. Regis. St. John's in Oxford. against
Brickenden.

Pledge.
Debt lies against him that becomes pledge without deed, Not. br. 122. K. 18.
Edw. 3. 13. pl. 7. Finchden.

A. borrowed of B. 20 l. to pay it at Michaelmas, at which day D. prays B. to
take him for Debtor, and gives him day over and obliges him to pay it, by one
Tallie ensealed, Debt lies not against D. because A. was not by this
discharged, 44 Edw. 3. 21. pl. 23. Purveyor.


Purveyor contracts for fat wares for the king and makes a bill of receipt to
the use of the King, and for this obliges him to pay, but seals it not, he
shall be charged by Assumpsit, and the King by debt and by no other way, 8
Eliz. Dyer. Receivor.
230. pl. 56.

Debt lies against a Receivor which takes more then he ought, per 7 Edw. 6.
cap. 6. Lib. Successor.
intra. 191. B. sect. 1. com. 201. Stradlings case.

Abbot shall be charged with the borrowing of his predecessor if it come to the
use of his house, Not. br. 121. K. Lib. intra. 152. A. sect. 1.

The count shall be general, Coke. 7. part. 10. B. Vghtreds case. Society.


Praecipe societati Lombardiorum London mercatorum de Florentia, and this was
good, 19 Hen. Shrive under shrieve.
6. 80. pl. 11.

Debt upon an escape of one in execution upon an account, it lies per Westminster. 2.
cap. 11. and of the debtor, per 1 Rich. 2. cap. 12.

For not returning a Knight of the parliament, per 23 Hen. 6. cap. 15. the
count com. 118. Buckleys case. Lib. intra. 186. A. sect. 1.

Shrieve takes an obligation for an Appearance of the defendant which not
appears, yet debt lies not against the shrieve, by the plaintiff, Trin. 13.
Jac. com. Ban. Outlawed person.


It lies against a person Outlawed, Mich. 38. et. 39. of Eliz. com. Ban.
Banister. versus Trussell. No. Lib. intra. 248. A. 7 Hen. 6. 10.

For what things Debt lies.
Lent.
It lies for money lent to another, Not. br. 119. G.

Of a horse lent till such a day and then to give 10l. or the horse after the
day, debt lies for the one or the other. Not. br. 121. B.

A. borrowed money for the servant, debt lies not against the Master unless it
came to his use by his assent, Doct. et Stud. 137. A.

Baylment.
To deliver to redeliver debt lies, 28 Hen. 8. Dyer. 22. pl. 135. 11 Hen. 6.
39. pl. 31. 4 Edw. 3. 9. pl. 7. although the receipt be not by deed.

To deliver to redeliver over to another if it be not performed debt lies, 28
Hen. 8. Dyer. 22. pl. 135. 11 Hen. 6. 39. pl. 31. 42 Edw. 3. 9. pl. 7. Mich.
40. 41. Eliz. com. Ban. Brittons case.

But 6 Hen. 4. 8. pl. 33. if A. ought to pay an Annuity in fee. to B. and
deliver money to C. to pay to B. yet B. shall not have debt against C.

Contract.
Lease for life of another debt lies not for the Rent during the term, Coke.
4. part. 49. A. Ognels case.

But by the 32 Hen. 8. cap. 37. the executors or administrators shall have debt
during the estate for life, Coke. 4. part. 49. A.

But after the estate ended, debt lies, Coke. 4. part. 49. A.

So it is by the death of the Lessee, Coke. 4. part. 49. A.

Or by Limitation.

Or by condition. in deed 39 Ewd. 3. 22. pl. 11. Not. br. 120. H. Coke. 23. B.
6 Hen. 7. 3. 30 Edw. 3. 7. in Law. Statute Law. 19 Hen. Common 42. A. Law.
wast.

Lease for years by a bailey the master shall have debt for the Rent, Lib.
intra. 174. D. sect. 3.

Corporation made a lease for years rendering to P or 20. days after verdict,
it was moved that they showed not the deed, sed non allocatur because it was
after verdict, 2 good although they had brought debt for the rent for 6. years
ended to P. and not 20 days after, Mich. 9. Jac. Ban. Regis. Baldry. defendant
in debt by the Corporation of Brewers.

Bargainee of a reversion in debt for rent, ought to show in what court the
deed was enrolled, Mich. 9. Jac. Ban. Regis. Welby et Purley.

Agistment.
Debt lies for the agistments for Cattle for so long time as they went, Lib.
intra. 150. A. sect. 1. count Lib. intra. 151. A. sect. 1.

Marriage money.
A. promises 20 1. to B. to marry his daughter, B. shall have debt, Not. 120.
K. count Lib. intra. 178. A. sect. 1. 37 Hen. 6. 8. pl. 18. 16 Hen. 3.
prohibition 22.

But if he promise 20l. in marriage with his daughter he shall not have debt
but sue in court christian, Not. br. 50. S. 16 Hen. 3. pro. 22. vide Regist 46.
B.

But if it be by deed. then see, 45 Edw. 3. 24.

Regula.
Bracton. Lib. 5. cap. 16. Sic de rebus datis vel promissis ob causam
matrimonii principaliter, et sic de rebus quae accidunt matrimonio ut si
pecunia promissa fuerit, ob causam matrimonii, quia ejusdem juris id est, et
jurisdictonis esse debet accessorium cujus est principale

Partition.
Partion, one promises the other 20 l. for equality of partition, debt lies
for it, Not. br. Rent upno a personal thing.
122. H. 14 Edw. 3. Debt. 137.

If a persoual thing be leased rendering rent debt lies for it, Coke. 3. part.
22. A. Walkers case.

Salary.
Attorney shall have debt for his fees and for fees of counsel, and costs of
suite, Not. br. 121. L. Count Lib. intra. 202. B. sect. 6.

A counselor shall have debt for his fees, 3 Hen. 6 33. pl. 26. 21 Hen. 6. 4.
pl. 6. but then he ought to count that he was of his counsel or was ready, 37
Hen. 8. B.

But 31 of Hen. 6. 9. B. Fortescue. sergeant at Law shall not have debt for his
fees.

Servant.
Shall have debt for his salary, Coke. 9. part. 87. 3 Hen. 6. 42. 11 Hen. 6.
48. although it be to do his service beyond the sea, Not. br. 120. E.

The Count, Lib. intra. 201. D. sect. 1.

Steward.
Steward retained by word shall have debt, 8 Eliz. Dyer. 248. pl. 79. Coke. 4.
part. 30. A.

Count for a chapleine, Lib. intra. 153. B. sect. 11.

Count for a Priest, Lib. intra. 202. B. sect. 5.

Count for one retained, etc. Lib. intra. 203. B. sect. 12.

Surgery.
I. promise to a Surgeon 40 s. to cure B. he shall have debt because it is a
good contract, 37 Hen. 6. 9. A. Moyle. Tabling.


Debt lies against him that Tables with me, 27 Edw. 3. 87. pl 37. 9 Edw. 4. 1.
The count lib. intra. 153. B. sect. 10. et 177. D. sect. 1.

Jailer shall have debt for tabling of a Prisoner, Coke. 9. part. 87. B. 28
Hen. 6. 4. pl. 21.

Inkeeper shall have debt for Lodging or victual, 39 Hen. 6. 18. pl. 24.

Tabling. and physic.
Physician shall have debt for tabling and physic, Lib. intra. 187. B. sect.
1. vide the count there.

Tailor.
If I. put my Cloth to a Tailor to make a garment he shall have a special
action for the putting of the cloth is a sufficient contract in Law, Coke. 8.
part. 147. Carpenters case.

But not a general action of debt without a contract in deed, ibidem

Vendition.
If I buy a Manor Debt lies for the money yet I shall not have it before
Livery, 37 Hen. 6. 8. pl. 18. Prisot.

I bargain for a horse Debt lies for the money, 14 Hen. 8. 19. br. contract,
15. Coke. 4. part. 94. B. Slades case.

If a man makes an obligation for debt due by contract debt* lies not upon the
contract, Not. br. 121. M. Coke. 6. part.

Because the obligation drowns the contract.

Upon an emisset of several ways, the count, No. Lib. intra. 125. B.

Servant.
If I. give authority to my bailey or servant to buy for me debt lies against
me, Not. br 120. G. Doct. et Stud. 137. A. 6 Eliz. Dyer. 130. pl. 56. 2 Rich.
2. Debt 13.

And so if he bought it without command if it come to the use of the Master by
his assent, Doct. et Stud. 137. A.

And likewise if he bought it in his own name and it comes to the use of his
Master it lies against his Master, ibidem.

So if the bailey which used to sell, sold a horse for twelve bushels of wheat,
this is good and the master shall have debt, 27 Assiz. pl. 5.

The servant sels, the Master agrees, this is the sale of the Master, debt
lies, 27 Hen. 8. 25. B. Fithams.

A factor receives money and gives a bill of exchange if the Master accept the
bill by it he becomes debtor by the custom, Trin. 43 Eliz. com. ban.

Wife.
The wife buys a thing the husband agrees this is the emption of the husband,
27 Hen. 8. 25. B. Fittiams.

Voluntary per Crier.
One condemned taken in Westminster hall kept by a crier assigned which suffers
him to escape, debt lies not, 1, because it was no prison, 2 because he had no
command by writ, 33 Hen. 6. 55. pl. 50.

Shrieve.
If a prisoner escape by assent although the shrieve take him again yet debt
lies, Coke. 3. part. 44. Boytons case. 19. Hen. 4. 10.

Unless the shrieve brought one per habeas Corpus then if he had him at the
day it suffices Coke. 3. part. 44. Boytons case.

Unless the party be in execution, Coke. 5. part. 89. Frosts case. 7. Hen. 4.
30.

Or upon a capias ad satisfaciendum although the writ be not returned, Coke. 3.
part. 52. Rigwayes case.

And if it be returned and had not the body debt lies, 7 Hen. 4. 11. br.
return 107.

A writ of privilege for a Burges of Parliament the shrieve suffers him at
large debt lies not, 36 Hen. 8. Dyer. 6. pl. 17. 1. Jac. Negl^gent escape per
Shrieve.


If one be taken by a capias utlagat. after the year and escape debt lies,
Coke. 5. part. 89. Frosts case. 88. B. Garnons case. vide 7 Hen. 6. 5. in
forgery.

The ancient Shreive makes no mention of one in execution this is an escape in
the old shreive, but not in the new, but if the old shrieve dye the other ought
to take notice, but if the escape be in the vacancy debt lies not, Coke. 3.
part. 71. and 72. Westbyes case. 10 Edw. 3. 375. pl. 28.

If one be in execution yet debt lies against the shrieve, 7 Eliz. Dyer. 241.
pl. 47. 16 Edw. 4. 3. pl. 7.

The Plaintiff and chief Justice assent for one time and after he suffers an
escape debt lies, 10 Eliz. Dyer. 275. pl. 46.

A capias upon a recognizance in chancery the party taken escapes, debt lies
Coke. 8. part. 142. Druries case

The count was that 6 were in execution and escaped and the doubt was whether
they might count for one only and by the better opinion it was good, Crook. 26
Hen. 7. 67. pl. 11.

If one be marshall whether it be by right or Marshall.
wrong debt lies against him, 39 Hen. 6. 33. A.

Count that he was in execution in C. and removed and committed to the Marshall
which suffers him to escape debt lies, 38. Hen. 6. 28 pl. 10.

Deputy.
Deputy of a Marshall suffers an escape, debt lies against him, 11 Eliz. Dyer.
278. pl. 5.

Mayor de Staple.
Debt lies against a Mayor of the Staple upon a recognizance taken before him,
5 Hen. 6. 11 Hen. 6. 49. B. 12 Hen. 6. 2. pl. 9.

The count, Lib. intra. 171. D. sect. 6.

Lord de Franchize
Deane and chapter of Paul's having return of writ and making a bailey that
suffers an escape Action lies not against the deane and chapter because they
are not baylyes, Pasch. 14 Eliz. com. ban.

Grannt. penalty.
1. Nomine poenae granted this is casual and debt lies for it, Not. br. 120.
M. 2 Hen. 8. 8. Dyer. 24. pl. 149.

And this is but hac vice if there be no other words, 32. Hen. 6. 10. A.
Billinge.

And so upon any grant hac vice certain or uncertayn.

Annuity.
2. Annuity or rent charge granted for years debt lies not during the term, But
the 5 Edw. 4. 42. B. debt lies.

But against a customer it lies if it be to be paid out of the customs of L.
after delivery of a Liberate, Not. br. 121. F.

It lies for executors or administrators of the Grantee per 32. Hen. 8. cap. 37.

And after the term ended it lies for the Grantee Lib. intra. 151. C. sect. 1.

For Life.
3. Annuity for life debt lies not for this during life, 19 Hen. 6. 42. A. 37
Hen. 6. 35. A.

But against a customer it lies, Not. br. 121. F.

Also if a Parson or Prebende, etc. has such annuity and resign or be
despossessed it lies for the arrerages, Coke. 4. part. 48. B. Ognels case. For
by his resignation he is merely personal.

So his executors shall have debt by the common law, Coke. 4. part. 49. A. 22
Eliz. Dyer. 37. pl. 62. Coke. 10. part. 61. B.

But if it be a Rent-charg seck or service debt lies not for any so long as the
estate continues Coke. 4. part. 49. A. Ognels case.

Although it have Continuance but to a special intent, Coke. 7. part. 39. B.

But after it be determined debt lies for the party or his executor, Coke. 4.
part. 49. Ognels case. Not. br. 121. E. Coke. 4. part. 49. Ognels case. 27 Hen.
6. 1. pl. 4. because the realty is resolved in the personality.

In Tail.
4. Annuity in Tail general or special debt lies not during the annuity,
Coke. 4. part. 48. B.

So of a Bent-seck, service or charg.

But if the estate be determined, quaere.

But by the 32. Hen. 8. cap. 37. the executor or administrator shall have debt
for the Arrerages.

Annuity or Rent in Fee.
Annuity in fee during the annuity debt lies not, Coke. 4. part. 48. B. 6 Hen.
4. 7. pl. 33.

Unless it be in a special case as when a parson or prebend resign, Coke. 4.
part. 49. A. Not. br. 121. D. 19 Hen. 6. 41. and 42. Not. br 121. H.

So if a parson dies his executors shall have debt, Not. br. 120. L. Coke. 4.
part. 49. A. 37 Hen. 6. 8. pl. 18.

And by the 32 Hen. 8. cap. 37. the executors or administrators of every one.

But after the Annuity determined every one shall have debt, Coke. 4. part. 49.
A. 45 Edw. 3. 45. execution 71

Parliament. Ban. Regis. Judgment given. Superior. Chancery. In Court of

Judgment given in debt for the principal.
If a man brings debt, upon a recovery in com. Ban. he ought to bring it in
Middlesex, wherethe record is, because it is the Original, but a scire facias
to execute one Judgment shall be where the Original was, because it ought to
follow it, Hill. 9. Jac. Ban. Regis. Musgrave versus Wharton.

Arrerages recovered in a scire facias upon Judgment in annuity against the
predecessors debt lies upon it, Not. br. 122. E. 22 Edw. 4. 1. pl. 6.

Debt recovered in court of Pypowders, and debt brought upon it in com. ban.
super tenorem recordi, and good, 7 Hen. 6. 19. For damages and costs.


If a man recover damages in w^st he shall have debt for the damages, Not. br.
122. C. 43 Edw. 3. 2. pl. 5. the count Lib. intra. 197. C. sect. 15.

Debt for damages in Assize 32 Hen. 6. 29. pl. 23. but then this ought to agree
with the Record, the count, Lib. intra. 194. D. sect. 7.

So for damages in a Mort-dauncester, 46 Edw. 3. 25. pl. 10.

The Plaintiff in com. ban. is nonsuited and the record removed by writ of
error the defendant shall have debt for his costs, 29 Hen. 8. Dyer. 32. pl. 5.

Damages recovered in ancient demeasne and the tenor of the record was removed
by Cerc^orari, debt lies upon it for the damage, 39 Hen. 6. 3. pl. 5. count
Lib. intra. 195. C. sect. 11.

Damages recovered before the Mayor of Hull debt lies there, 11 Hen. 4. 12.

Fine.
Debt lies for a fine, Coke. 8. part. 41. B. Greisleys case. 7 Hen. 6. 2. B.

Amerciament.
Debt lies for an amerciament in a Leete, Lib. intra. 151. B. sect. 1. 23 Hen.
8. br. Leete. 37. The count Lib. intra. 151. B.

Debt. lies in a Court barron, No. Lib. intra. Judgment out of Court as statute.
118. B. sect. 1.

Debt lies upon a Statute Merchant, Staple and according to the 23 Hen. 8. Not.
br. 122. C. 11. Hen. 6. 49. pl. 7.

Recognizance.
Debt lies upon a Recognizance, Not. br. 122. C. 11 Hen. 6. 49. pl. 7. Eliz.
Dyer. 306. pl. 63. The count Lib. intra. 192. B. sect. 1.

Or upon the tenor of the Recognizance, 39 Hen. 6. 3. pl. 5. 22 Eliz. Dyer.
369. pl. 52.

So upon a Recognizance taken before the Mayor of Hull. 36 Hen. 6. 2. pl. 2.

Debt brought upon a Recognizance after the Recognizance and before the
enrollment and good, Passc. 43. Eliz. com. ban.

Account at the common law.
Debt lies upon arrerages of Account at the Common law, the count Lib. intra.
149. A. sect. 1.

Also a Bailey shall have debt upon the surplusage of account, Not. br. 121. I.
38. Hen. 6. 5. 19 Edw. 2. Debt. 176.

He ought to count the place and day where the Auditors were assigned, Hill. 32
Eliz. com. ban. Lord Dacres case.

But if the Lord will not hear his account he has no remedy for the
surplusage, 7 Edw. 3. 12. per Herle.

But not by a Receiver, 38. Hen. 6. 5. pl. 14. Mich. 12. Jac. ban. Regis.
Countess de Suffolk. versus Floyde.

But a receiver for Merchandise shall have it, 38 Hen. 6. 5. Prisott et Moyle.

Arbitriment.
Debt lies upon an Arbitrament, Not. br. 121. G. Coke. 9. part. 92. B. the
count Lib. intra. 153. C. sect. 1.

By laws or ordinances.
Debt lies upon an ordinance or by law, Coke. 5. part. 64. A.

A Pain upon one in a leete to reform a nuisance and afterward it is presented
that it is not done the Lord shall have debt, 23. Hen. 8. br. Leete 37.

Penalty inflicted upon one in London per the common counsel debt lies for it
in Ban. Regis. Matter in law, as for* Aid.
Mich. 9. Jac. ban. Regis.

Debt lies for the daughter for Aid to marry her, Not. br. 83. A. et 122. G.
For an Annuity against a Customer etc. after delivery of a Liberate.


A man having an annuity of the King, delivers a writ to a customer which has
assets he shall have debt, Not. br. 121. F.

So if he deliver a Talle to a customer, 27 Hen. 6. 9. pl. 1.

So if he deliver a Talle to a collector of tenths and fifteens, 37 Hen. 6. 15.
pl. 5.

Pro rationabili part bonorum.
Debt pro rationabili part bonorum where the custom gives such part, Not. br.
122. L. 3 Edw. 3. Debt 156.

The count was that the son or daughter which is not heir nor preferred in
the life of the father shall have a reasonable part and shows the things to
the value, etc. Lib. intra. 564. B. sect. 1,

But shall not have this writ but where such custom is, 40 Edw. 3. 38. pl. 13.
Mowbray. 7 Edw. 4. 20. pl. 23.

For it cannot be founded upon Magna charta cap. 8. because it is but only
foreprised, Regist. orig. 141. B. 30 Edw. 3. 26. A. Seton.

But other Books say it lies at Commonlaw, Not. br. 122. L. Glanvil Lib. 12.
cap. 20. 17 Edw. 3. 9. pl. 29.

And the account is upon the common law, No. Lib. intra. 565. A. sect. 2.

So debt lies where the custom is that the heir shall have the principal
goods, 30 Edw. 3. 2. pl. 9. 39 Edw. 3. 6. pl. 24. et fol. 9. pl. 15.

Executor shall have debt for a relief because For a relief per executor.
it is but an improvement of the service, Coke. 4. part. 49. B. 34 Edw. 1.
Avowry, 233. 11 Hen. 6. 15- pl. 4.

And it is a chattell to the executor, 34 Edw. 3. Advowry, 233.

But the Lord shall not have debt, Coke. 4. part. 49. B. 7 Hen. 6. 13. For it
is no chattell to the Lord, 34 Edw. 1. Avowry 233.

For Toll.
Toll shall be recovered by debt, 20 Hen. 7. 1. pl. 2. but vide librum et
quaere.

For Escuage*
Debt lies for Escuage after that it is assessed per parliament for then it is
a duty certain, Crook. 133. pl. 111.

Simple. Obligation conditional.
Debt lies upon a simple obligation count, Lib. intra. 178. B. sect. 1.

Vide versus Attorney vel sarvientum ad legem, fol. 174. D. sect. 5. et 6.

Debt upon a bill to pay within a month after that the Plaintiff shall come
from Jerusalem, he needs not give notice to the defendant because he is bound
to pay it at his peril, Hill. 9. Jac. Ban. Regis. Edmonds.

Obligation with condition to perform covenants, No. Lib. intra. 130. B. sect.
14.

Obligation to discharge and save harmeless the shrieve of all escapes of
persons in execution, A good breach to show that one was in execution, per
capias, etc. and suffered him at large without showing 1 that he was at large,
2 without giving notice and request to save him harmless 3 without showing
that the capias was returned, Trin. 12. Jac. com. ban. Norton versus Smyth.

Upon a bill obligatory the count, Lib. intra. 178, B. sect. 1. 2. 3.

Bill obligatory with condition, Lib. intra. 178. C. sect. 4.

Debt upon an obligation made in England to be paid in Flanders, Lib. intra.
158. C. sect. 1.

Debt lies upon a Tallee sealed, Not. br. 122. I. 2 Rich. 2. Debt 4. vide 44
Edw. 3. 24. pl. 23.

The writ in Debt, 1. In the county, 2. in Com. Ban.
County.
Rex, etc. praecipimus tibi quod justicies A quod just et sine dilatione
reddat B. XXl. quas ei debet, ut dicitur, sicut rationabiliter monstrare
poteret, quod ei reddere debeat, ne amplius inde clamorem audiamus Pro defectu
Justitiae, etc. Regist. orig. 139. A. Not. br. 119. H.

In comitatu Pro debito semper dicitur quas ei debet, tantum et pro catallis
detinet tantum, Regist. orig, 139. B.

But for executors always in the detinet, ibidem. Administrator.


If debt be by administrators all must be named, Regist. orig. 140. A.

The Writ shall be Detinet only, Regist. orig. 139. B.

If one recover against administrators, and bring debt upon the Record, the
writ shall be detinet only, 11 Hen. 4. 56. pl. 2. vide 11 Hen. 6. 7. 16. 39.
For by Newton, fol. 37. debet imports his proper debt being upon his own
contract, 20 Hen. 6. 5. A. Fortescue.

Husband and wife.
The writ shall be debet et detinet eis, Coke. 5. part. 36. A. Walkots case. 12
Hen. 4. 1. pl. 1. 7 Hen. 7. 2. B.

But the count shall be special, 7 Hen. 7. 2. B.

So in debt against them for debt due before Coverture, 7 Hen. 7. 2. B.

Against a collector.
Bill against a collector after that he has accounted there ought to be nuper
collector, 15 Edw. 4. 27.

By executors.
Debt per executors the writ shall be detinet only, although the duty accrue in
their time, Coke. 5. part. 31. B. Hargraves case. Not. br. 119. M. Regist.
orig. 140. A. for goods sold by them 19 Hen. 8. 8. 11 Hen. 6. 36. A. 20 Hen. 6.
5. B. for Rent due in their time.

If they sell a thing and take an obligation, 17 Edw. 3. 64. pl. 78. 25 Edw. 3.
40. pl. 7. and this is to the use of the Testator.

Et Regist. orig. 138. B. 9 Hen. 6. 11. B. 20 Hen. 6. 4. B. Paston.

In ancient time in such case it was in the debet and detinet but not at this
day because that debet supposes a property which the executor has not.

All executors ought to join in debt although that some refuse the
Administration, Regist. orig. 140. B. 22 Edw. 3. 19. pl. 8. 7. 41 Edw. 3. 22.
pl. 10. 21 Edw. 4. 24. 36 Hen. 6. 8. Coke. 9. part. 37. Hensloes case. 24. Edw.
3. 40. B. Thorpe. 19 Hen. 6. 31.

Vide tamen, 38 Edw. 3. 9. pl. 7. L. where an executor sold goods and brought
debt sole and it was awarded good.

Executor and an executor of an executor join in debt and good, 7 Edw. 3. 261.
pl. 22.

But the, 28 Edw. 3. 92. pl. 11. Wilby. this is not Law. For 29 Edw. 3. 49. 23.
the surviving executor shall have it sole.

Wife executrix.
Wife executrix Debt by her and her husband the writ shall suppose both
executors, 22 Hen. 6. 49. pl. 8.

Feme covert executrix shall not have debt without the husband and sovereign,
8 Edw. 3. 330. pl. 48. 10 Edw. 3. 381. pl. 63. 21 Hen. 6. 30. pl. 17. Marke^am.
Regist. orig. 140.

Against executors.
The writ shall be detinet only, Not. br. 119. M. Regist. orig. 139. B.

But for Rent due in the time of the executor it shall be in the debet et
detinet, Coke. 5. 31. Hargraves case. 7 Edw. 6. 81.

A man being executor of his own wrong takes administration, quaere how he
shall be sued, Crook. 127. pl. 91. A.

It suffices to name them only that be administrators, Regist. orig. 140. A,
et B. 19 Hen. 6. 31. Coke. 9. part. 37. Hensloes case. 33 Hen. 6. 38. pl. 15.

Debt against an executor which pleads another they both may plead another but
the former only cannot, 29. Edw. 3. 11. pl. 32.

Debt lies against an executor of right and wrong 39 Hen. 6. 45. pl. 19.

But not against an executor and executor of an executor, 41 Edw. 3. 13. pl. 3.

Two executors administer and intermary debt lies against both 22 Hen. 6. 59.
pl. 12.

Heir.
The heir ought to be named, 30 Hen. 6. 5. pl. 2.

But Regist. orig. 140. A. he was named heir in the count only and yet good,

He was named heir apparent and it was erroneous, Pasch. 35. Eliz. Ban. Regis
242. Audleys case.

It shall be against him in the debet et detinet and not in the detinet only
because he has assets in his own right, Coke. 5. part. 36. Walkots case.
Regist. orig. 140. A. com. 441. A. Pepys case.

Ordinary.
Praecipe A. epi scop. London. ad cujus manus bona et catalla quae fuerunt B.
qui obiit intestat. ut dicitur devenerunt quod just et sine, etc. reddat, etc.
C. solidos quos idem B. ei debuit et praedictus epis cop. ei injuste detinet ut
dicet et nisi, etc. Regist. orig 141. A. Not. br. 120. D.

Et ibidem vide the writ against an executor of the ordinary.

But it lies not for the Ordinary, Not. br. 120. D. Coke. 9. part. 39. Hensloes
case. tamen vide, the writ for the Ordinary in the Regist. orig. 141. A. Nota.


Nota when a man demands money it shall be debet et detinet, Not. br. 119. G.

And if it be for any other thing it shall be in the detinet only, Not. br.
119. G. Regist. orig. 139. B. 34 Hen. 6. 12. pl. 23.

And the writ shall make mention of the value, 17 Edw. 3. 48. pl. 17. 29 Edw.
3. 39. pl. 14. et fol. 45. pl. 6.

And if it be for silver or other things then it shall say 10 l. quas ei debet
et injuste detinet, et 10 l. quarters of corn quae ei injuste detinet, Not.
br. 152. B. 3 Hen. 4. 13. pl. 20. 11 Hen. 6. 48. pl. 6. 12 Hen. 6. 1. pl. 3.
vide 39 Hen. 6. 34. pl. 46. debt for 300 l.

A man cannot demand 10 l. by one writ and 10 l. by another where the contract
was for XX1. 1 Hen. 5. 6. B.

For in Mich. 14. Jac. Ban. Regis. in the case of the Baylyes of Ipswich
Houghton Justice said that A. was indebted to the King. in 3000 l. the King
granted to B. 1000 l. parcel of it, yet B. shall not have debt for the 1000 l.
as was adjudged in the Chequer, Int. York et Allen.

A. was bound in 6 l. Flemmish, quaere what writ he shall have, 34 Hen. 6. 12.
pl. 23. 29 Edw. 3. 19. pl. 5.

For Lib. intra. 158. C. sect. 1. the writ was 28 l. and the count of the bill,
19 l. 16 s. Flemmish which is 14 l. English, and for the Remnant, etc.

The Process in Debt, 1. before Appearance, 2. after appearance.
At the common law the process was but a summons Attachment and distress in
finite, Coke. 12. A. Harberts case.

But by 25 Edw. 3. cap. 17. capias was given for it yet the process is summons
Attachment and distress, 3. capias and one exigend. 14. Hen. 6. 20. A.

But if debt be in the county per Justices and the bailey return a nihil habet
and afterward this is removed quaere if a capias lies, 3 Hen. 5. 4.

Nota.
Nota that a capias lies not upon a Recognizance, 23 Hen. 7. 100. pl. 1. Crook.

Nor against a Peer of the Realm Coke. 6. part. 52, B. 11 Hen. 4, 15. 3 Hen.
6, 48. 29 Edw. 3, 30, pl. 40 et 42, pl. 3. 5 Edw. 4. 108. B.

But if a Bushop of Wales or Ireland be sued, upon a nihil habet returned A
capias lies, ibidem.

Account.
The Bar in Debt.
For arrerages of account.
Debt lies for arrerages of account that he owes nothing a good bar, Lib.
intra. 149. B. sect. 2.

2. before auditors.
And this may be by wager in law because it is within the statute, 22 Hen. 6.
35. pl. 53. 9 Hen. 5. 3. pl. 9. 43 Edw. 3. 1. pl. 3.

And so if it be before an auditor, Coke. 10. part. 103. A. 4 Hen. 6. 25. pl.
3. 20 Hen. 6. 16. pl. 4. 13 Hen. 7. 3. B. Conesby.

2. before auditors.
If it be for arrerages of account before auditors, imprisonment by auditors a
good bar; but then he ought to be committed forthwith, 27 Hen. 6. 8. pl. 7.
Coke. 8. part. 119 B. com. 17.

Non computa vit a good bar, 3 Mariae Dyer. 122. pl. 18.

Null tiel account, 34 Hen. 6. 22. A. Danby.

Arbitriment for arrerages of account no bar because one is matter of record, 3
Hen. 4. 5. pl. 23. 4 Hen. 6. 17. 6 Hen. 4. 6. pl. 28. 8 Hen. 5. 3. pl. 13.
Hull, 3 Hen. 6. 55. A.

Auditors discharged by the plaintiff a good bar, Lib. intra. 150. A. sect. 9.

Obligation made to the plaintiff for arerages no bar, 11 Hen. 4. 79.

Payment in another county a good bar, Lib. intra. 150. A. sect. 10.

That he owes nothing per patriam, a good bar, Lib. intra. 150. A. sect. 1. 4
Mariae. Dyer. 145. pl. 63.

That he owes nothing by the law no bar, because Auditors are Judges of
record, 2. cap. 11. Coke. 103. A. Debounds case. 4 Hen. 6. 17. 8 Hen. 6. 5. 14
Hen. 19. pl. 21. 9 Hen. 5. 3. pl. 9.

But the Plaintiff may be examined and if it be found that he is not in
arrerages the defendant may wage his law, per statute, 5 Hen. 4. cap. 8. Coke.
10. part. 103. A. 8 Hen. 6. 10 et 15. 19 Hen. 6. 43. pl. 90. 20 Hen. 6. 32.
Ashton.

And if the plaintiff or his attorney refuse to be examined the defendant shall
wage his law, 33 Hen. 6. 24. pl. 5.

But if the executor brings debt for arrerages of account in vita testatoris he
shall not be examined, but his Attorney shall but not upon oath, 3 Hen. 6. 40.
pl. 2, 19 Hen. 6. 8. 10 Hen. 6. 20. 34 Hen. 6. 32. Ashton. 20 Edw. 4. 3. pl. 24.

But 21 Hen. 6. 4. pl. 10. the executor was examined but not precisely.

So if another brought such action against an executor he shall not be
examined, 20 Edw. 4. 3. pl. 14.

So if it be found that they submit themselves to arbitriment so that they were
not Auditors but arbitrators they shall wage their law, 22 Hen. 6. 41. pl. 13.

Lord.
The lord shall say that he owes nothing and was by his law, Westminster. 2 cap. 11,
does not extend to the Lord, 14 Hen. 6, 24. 22 Hen. 6, 41. 38 Hen. 6, A. 29
Edw. 3, 26. pl. 20. Coke. 9, part. 87, A. Pinchons case.

The defendant alleges before auditors that he delivered to the plaintiff one
Statute Merchant in leive of the sum, the plaintiff wages his law, 30 Edw. 3.
4. pl. 19.

Acquittance of the last day shall discharge all arrerages, 11 Hen. 4. 24. 10
Eliz. Dyer. 271. pl. 26.

The Lessee pleads the command of the Lessor to repair the house with the rent
because it was decayed this is no good plea because it is wast, 34 Hen. 6. 17.
14 Hen. 4. 27. pl. 35. 11 Rich. 2. Bar.

But if the grande timber be in decay perchance it may be a good bar, ibidem.

The Lessee was Advocate in the spiritual court, the Lessor promises that he
shall keep the Rent for his fees, this is no bar, for stoppage is no plea, but
he has a good ground to have an Assumpsit, Mich. 9. Jac. Ban. Regis. Jarvis
versus Lea.

The Lessee pleads that the Lessor entered before the day and ejected him a good
bar, 27 Hen. 6. 10. pl. 6. 46 Edw. 3. 1. pl. 1. Lib. intra. 175. D. sect. 10,
11., 12.

A good bar to say that the Lessor entered before his day without any more, 34
Hen. 6. 21. pl. 40.

So if the Lessor enter but in part a good bar, Coke. 3. part. 22. B. Walkers
case.

But if the Lessee enter again before the day of payment no bar.

So if the Lessor cuts the trees no bar because the Lessor ejects not the
Lessee, 33 Eliz.

Entry by a stranger which has a better title a good bar, Perkins 163. Lib.
intra. 176. A. sect. 13. 45 Edw. 3. 8. pl. 10.

But not for arrerages due before the entire, 9 Hen. 6. 17. B. Cottesmore. 19
Hen. 6. 42. B. Paston. 20 Hen. 6. 20. pl. 15.

Debt in com. M. where the land is in com. E. levied by distress good, without
saying more, 4 Hen. 6, 5, pl. 12. 22 Hen. 6, 31, pl. 19. 28 Hen. 6, 6, pl. 2.
Although the Lease be by Indenture 4 Hen. 6, 5. pl. 12. 18 Hen. 6, 17. A. per 2
Justices, 11 Hen. 7, 4. pl. 16.

But if it be in the same county where the land is then it ought to conclude
that he owed nothing because the country may have notice whether he did or not,
28 Hen. 6, 6, pl. 2. 33 Hen. 6, 4, pl. 12.

But the 9 Edw. 3. ^3, 4. pl. 16. Herle, it is good without such conclusion.

Debt upon a Lease for Tithes levied by distress no bar because there is
nothing subject to distress, 22 Hen. 6. 35. pl. 5^. 11 Hen. 4* 40. br. debt
234.

A good bar that the Lessor distrained and sold the distress for the rent by
the assent of the defendant, 2 Rich. 2. debt 235.

Payment in another county a good bar without saying more, 22 Hen. 6. 36. pl.
1. 34 Hen. 6. 17. B. Moyle, 9 Hen. 5. 2. pl. 6. 11 Hen. 7. 4. pl. 16. 1 Hen. 5.
6. et 7. 20 Hen. 6. 16. B. 22 Hen. 6. 35. pl. 53.

For otherwise it shall be tried where the writ is brought, 4 Hen. 6. 5. pl.
12.

To say that the Lessor covenanted to repayr the house or that the custom is
that he should repayr it, and did not do it, this is no bar because it is but
a covenant, but if the lease be that the lessee repaired it and paid the rent
this is a good bar, that the Lessor did not repayr it, 27 Hen. 6. 10. pl. 6.

But a lease by indenture and that the lessee repaired the house at the cost of
the lessor a good plea that he did expend the rent in repayring of the house, 2
Rich. 2. 235.

That it was upon a condition and upon the breach of the condition the Lessor
entered before there was any thing in arrear no plea for he ought to answer the
debet, Crook. 153. pl.

Surrender before the day a good bar, Lib. intra. 176. C. sect. 17. Contract
personal.


Accord a good plea Coke. 6. part. Blakes case. Lib. intra. 205. C. sect. 11.

Servant.
Payment to the servant no bar unless the servant was commanded by his master
to receive it or that the money came to the use of his master by his assent,
Doct. et Student. 138. A.

Lease for years of a stock of Cattle, or other Rent upno a personal thing.
personal thing rendering rent at several days debt lies not till all the
days be incurred, Coke. 3. part. 22. A. Walkers case.

That he owes nothing by the law a good Salary for a Counselor.
bar, 1 Hen, 6. 1. pl. 3. 9* Edw. 4. 1.

Attorney.
The defedant shall not wage his law because the court compel him to be

Servant.
That he departs his service within the term a good bar, 40 Edw. 3. 25. pl. 27.

That he discharged him of the service within the term to which he agreeed a
good bar, 10 Hen. 6. 23. pl. 78.

That he retained him not modo, forma, etc. a good bar, 38 Hen. 6. 22. pl. 41.

Payment without specialty is not good in debt by a servant retained in
husbandry, 40 Edw. 3. 21. pl. 27.

And so if one be retained but not according to the statute the Master may wage
his law in debt for the salary, Coke. 9. part. 87. and 88. Pinchons case. 3
Hen. 6. 42. pl. 13. 11 Hen. 6. 48. 4 Hen. 6. 19. B. 2 Hen. 4. 14. 39 Hen. 6.
18. pl. 24. 38 Hen. 6. 22. B.

But he may not plead that the servant demands 40 s. per annum, the statute
allows not this because he was not retained according to it, 11 Hen. 6. 10.
pl. 20.

So if it be retained in all occupations although that husbandry be
Comprehended within it.

If a general receiver retain one by deed yet the Master may plead that he
owes him nothing by the law, 28 Hen. 8. Dyer. 20. pl. 12. 4.

If one be retained in husbandry although he be not compellable to serve, yet
his Master shall not wage his law, 38 Hen. 6. 22. B. pl. 4. Steward.


A. retaynes B. to be his Steward of his court for one year or more he shall
have debt although the retayner be by word but not for an annual pension
unless the retayner be by deed, Crook. 1 Hen. 8. 158. pl. 6.

He cannot plead to the Country for part and wage his law for the other; but

upon it as a statute, Hill. 9. Jac. Ban. Regis. Fox versus Brook.

No debt in bar for arrerages of account before Auditors because the sum

Nullum fecerunt Arbitrium a good bar because this lies in notice of the

But if he plead such a plea he cannot rejoyne afterward and say that the

The arbitrators gave no notice no bar unless the submission be so.

Obligation simple Accord.
Debt upon an obligation, accord with satisfaction no bar, because the duty
being certain ought to be avoided by matter of as high a nature, Coke. 6. part.
44. A. Blakes case.

But if the duty accrue not until some subsequent act, there accord with
satisfaction a good plea, Coke. 6. part. 44. A.

Acquittance.
A. obliged to B. in 100l. shows 3 acquittances 1, of 10l. 2, of 20l. and 3,
of 20l. which amount to the receipt of 50l. parcel of the 100. in which he was
bound to pay 50l. this a good bar because it appears that it was but 50l.
principal debt, 43 Edw. 3. 31. pl. 26.

Attachment.
Forreyne attachment in London a good bar as it seems, No. Lib. intra. 139. C.
sect. 20. 22 Hen. 6. 47. pl. 2.

But a legacy cannot be attached, because it may not be due in respect of
payment of the Testators debts, Mich. 14. Jac. ban. Regis. Vaughans case.

Attainder
Attainder of felony no plea, Mich. 38, et 39. Eliz. com. ban. Banister versus
Trusselle.

Nil debet
Nil debet no plea because an obligation shall not be avoided by a nude
averment but by matter of as high a nature, Doct. et Student. 22.

Non composti mnetis
Non compos mentis pleaded by the party not adjudged, Trin. 37. Eliz. ban.
Regis. Strode Payment.
versus Marshall. vide 5 Edw. 3. 70.

A. is bound to pay his rent, there payment Obligation condionall.

When the original contract is for money Accord.
accord with satisfaction a good bar, Coke. 9. part. 79. A. Petoyes case. 22

But accord to a general receiver is no bar if he had not a special

The Defendant pleads he paid so much in full satisfaction, the which the

Conditions performed.
Conditions performed is a good bar, 41 Ed. 3. 10. pl. 7. and fol. 25. pl. 19.
Thorpe.

One pleads part of the Arbitriment, it shall be intended all, until the
contrary be showed. 2. The other may show the remnant absque hoc, Arbitriment.
that they arbitrated that only. 3. The other needs not to rejoyn to more,
because it shall be a departure from his Plea, Pasch. 12. Jac. Ban. Regis.
Linsey versus Ashton.

Condition to levy a fine.
Obligation with Condition to levy a fine upon Garnishment, the Shrieve returns
him garnished in Debt, he pleads that he was not by the Law, 28 Edw. 3. 100.
pl. 42. 29 Edw. 3. 44. pl. 4.

Deed pol.
A. enfeoffes B. by deed Poll, provided that he pay 20. l. to B. he may
re-enter, and is bound to perform all Covenants and Payments contained in the
deed Poll: he is not bound to pay the 20. l. for it is at his election to pay
it or lose the Land, Trin. 9 Jac. Ban. Regis. Briscoe versus Knight. Rott. 271.

A. is bound to pay a greater sum granted by Indenture to B. and to levy it
of his goods and Chattles: this is void, and therefore no bar, 41 Edw. 3. 7.
pl. 15. Belknap. 46. Edw. 3. 18. pl. 17. Belknap.

Condition.
A. conditions that B. shall lease to C. the Land in his Occupation, except the
Trees, this exception is not good, unless they were excepted in the Original
Lease, and then B. ought to show it, Mich. 15 Jac. Ban. Regis. Doors Case.

A. conditions that one shall make a Lease for 16. years, and he makes one for
ten years, if he live so long this is good; for it was employed before, Mich. 15
Jac. Ban. Regis. per Montague Chief Justice. Woolridge and Banbury.

Condition to deliver such a Lease as shall be devised by the Judge of the
Court of Audience. Non devisavit aliquid, etc. no bar, for he ought to procure
him to make one, Coke 5. part. 23. B. Lambs case. The pleading. No. Lib. Intra.
130. A.

Impossible condition.
A. is obliged to B. in 20. l. upon Condition to pay 10. l. to such a person at
such a place, and time, and that he would name him in his will, B. makes his
will and names none, the Executors shall not have it, for as yet the condition
is impossible, for he ought to be named in deed, Trin. 12. Jac. Com. Ban. Pease
and alii versus Mead. Mich. 11 Jac. Rott. 945.

The Defendant said that he made another obligation to the Plaintiff, the which
he did accept in satisfaction of the former: this is no bar, because it is but
a thing in Action, Mich. 12 Jac. Com. Ban. Rand. and Strut. Trn. 6. Jac. Com.
Ban. Rott. 10001. Lovelace.

Payment.
Payment, only the Condition a good Bar, Coke 8. part. 58. A. Beechers case.
But he to show the place, 5 Edw. 4. 141. B.

Payment of Parcel hanging the Writ is not good to abate the Writ, without
Acquittance, 3 Hen. 7. 3. pl. 12. 5 Hen 7. 10. pl. 15. 7. Edw. 4. 15. Vide 28.
Hen. 8. Dyer. 6. pl. 3.

A. is bound to B. in 10. l. and after the date is one clause that he shall pay
him 5. l. the Obligation is void, Payment there without acquittance is good, 30
Edw. 3. 3. pl. 12.

But Payment after the day is not good without acquittance, 46 Edw. 3. 29. pl.
23. 47 Edw. 3. 13. pl. 14. 5 Hen. 7. 41. pl. 5.

A. is bound to pay 20 quarters of Malt, and if he pay it not at the day, then
in 40 quarters; in Debt, for the 40 quarters he pleads payment without
acquittance but not in Debt for the 20 quarters. 28 Hen. 8. Dyer. 24. pl. 154.
1 Hen. 5. 7. A.

Three bound to pay their Rent, one pays it, the other plead payment without
acquittance, 45 Edw. 3. 4. pl. 9.

A. is bound by an obligation dated 17th of November. 12 Jac. with condition of
payment the 19th November next ensuing, per Curiam payment 19th November 13
Jac. is sufficient, for it shall not be intended 19th. November in the same
month. Mich. 13 Jac. Com. Ban. Price and Coe.

Conusee had Execution for 20. l. and by Indenture grants that if the Conusor
pay 8. l. at a day to come, it shall be void, this is a good discharge, 20
Assize. pl. 7.

Payment to a Deputy a good Bar, 42 Edw. 13. pl. 35.

Payment to the Bailey of a Bishop by his command a good Bar, 22 Edw. 4. 25. pl.
5.

But payment to a servant without command is no Bar, unless it comes to the use
of his Master, Doct. and Stud. 38. A.

Payment to a Creditor of the Obligee by his command is a good bar, 46 Edw. 3.
33. pl. 45. Perkins 145. A.

But then he ought to show that the Creditor was the Creditor of the Obligee,
27 Hen. 6. 6. pl. 1.

Condition to pay 20 l. to B. as soon as he comes to the Age of 21 years. 1. He
ought to show that he is of full years. 2. He ought to show the place where he
paid it, for otherwise there cannot be any tenure, Mich. 12 Jac. Ban. Regis.
Halse.

Permit.
Condition to permit one to enjoy, etc. he pleads that he did permit him and
good, 10 Eliz. Dyer. 279. pl. 6.

^etainer*
Defendant said that the Plaintiff was indebted to him, and that he commanded
him to retain it, a good bar, 22 Edward. 4. 25. 6 5.

^arr general to an obligation.

Acquittance.


Acquittance a good bar.

But an acquittance by a general Receiver without receipt of the Money is not
good, unless he be receiver by deed, and has authority to make acquittances,
Doct. and Stud. 137. B.

A. brought debt in ban. Regis. against B. and that depending, brought debt in
London, and had goods attached in the hands of C. and had Judgment upon them,
this is a good bar in debt, by B. against C. but if A. brings debt against B.
and after the debt is attached in London, and Judgment given there, if the
Creditor sue B. he cannot plead the Attachment in bar, because he might have
pleaded the action brought against him in Com. ban. Mich. 39, et 40. Eliz. com.
ban. Jaques, versus Lewkner.

Debt is attachable before the day in which it is payable because the debtor
debet although non detinet but an obligation made to perform covenants is not
attachable, Mich. 39, et 40. Eliz. com. ban. Beacher, versus Minors.

Coverture.
Coverture a good bar. Lib. intra. 168. B. sect. 1.

Infancy.

Non est factum.


Infancy a good bar, Lib. intra. 163 A. sect. 1.

Non est factum a good bar, but not if the deed be enrolled, 16 Hen. 5. B. 9
Hen. 6. 60. A Babington. 39 Hen. 6. 32. pl. 45.

When it is but voidable non est factum no plea, Coke. the 5. part. 119. A.
Whelpsdales case. 11 Hen. 7. 15.

When an obligation is made void by statute yet non est factum is no plea,
Coke. 2. part. 9. B. Thoroughgoods case.

When an obligation is once good and after and before, the plea be void, non
est factum may be pleaded, Coke. 5. part. 119. A. B. Whelpsdales case.

When 3 are bound seperatim, and the seal of one is broken the other cannot
plead non est factum because they are several obligations, Coke. 5. part. A.
Mathewsons case.

But it is not when 3 are bound without any more, Coke. 11. part. 28. B. Pigots
case. 3 Hen. 7. 5. Coke. 5. part. 23. A.

But if 2 be bound in debt against one only it cannot be pleaded, Coke. 5.
part. 119. A. Whelpsdales case.

Recovery.
Recovery in an inferior court of Record with execution a good bar, Coke. 6.
part. 45. B. Higgins case.

But without execution not, Coke. 6. part. 45. A.

Recovery is a good bar so long as it is in force, Coke. 3. part. 44. B.
Higgins case.

Release.
Release a good bar.

Two bound to B. which makes the wife of one his executrix and devises his
goods to her this is a good releas of the debt, for if the obligee make the
wife of the obligor his executrix this is a release in Law, because it is
suspended by the act of the party, Trin. 12. Jac. com. ban. Friar versus
Gildridg.

A release of all advantages in account a good bar, in debt upon an account,
9. Edw. 4. 49. Coke. 8. part. 152. A. Althams case.

A. is bound to B. to the use of C. the release of C. is a good bar, 36 Hen.
8. br. obligation 27.

^ymony.
Defendant said that the agreement was for the obtaining a benefice, this is
naught, 1 the statute makes the contract void, 2. It cannot be averred out of
it, Mich. 40 et 41 Eliz. com. ban. Gregory versus Olden.

Defendant pleads that the obligee accepted of a statute for the obligation
after the day, Statute.
this is no bar because the obligation is in force notwithstanding, Coke. 6.
part. 44. B. Higgins case.

Statute law.
The condition was to save the surety harmless no plea that the former bond
was usurious because the counter bond was not for payment of money, Mich. 40,
et 41. Eliz. com. ban. ban. Dowman versus Button.

The Judgment in debt.
Against an executor.
The Judgment, Lib. intra. 173. B. sect. 1.

Arrerages of account the executor pleads no such account or nothing in arrere
or outlary in the plaintiff and it is found against him, the Judgment shall be
de bonis Testatoris, 34 Hen. 6. 22. A. Danby.

A covenant broken after the death of the Testator the Judgment shall be de
bonis Testatoris, 15 Eliz. Dyer. 324. pl. 34.

Nothing in Arrere in debt for rent due in vita testatoris or no such lease,
the Judgment shall be de bonis testatoris, 34 Hen. 6. 22. A. Danby.

Accquittance or release pleaded and found against him if it be pleaded and
made to the executor the Judgment shall be general, 11 Hen. 6. 8. A. Danby.
34 Hen. 6. 24. A. Prisot.

Non assumpsit of the Testator to pay the debt the Judgment is of costs and
damages, of suit de bonis propriis if the Testator had not sufficient, No. Lib.
intra. 1. B. sect 1.

The executor found in a Cheft a grant of the next avoydance made to the
Testator and presentation there upon a Recovery in a quare impedit against him,
the Judgment shall be of his proper goods, 34 Hen. 6. 22. B. Prisot.

Coexecutor pleades and found against him, the Judgment shall be de bonis
testatoris, 9 Hen. 6. 44. 11 Hen. 6, 7. 34 Hen. 6. 32. A.

Confession of the Action by the executor the Judgment shall be general
against him, because he ought to have pleaded that he had not more then 20 s.
and against the other executor it shall be de bonis testatoris, 14 Hen. 4. 12.
pl. 1. Hull.

And by 33 Hen. 6. 2. it shall be of the goods of the testator if he has none
for damages of the goods of the executor that confesses the action.

But 4 Eliz. Dyer. 210. pl. 23. it shall be but de bonis testatoris against
both, 28 Hen. 6. 3. pl. 13. 40 Edw. 3. 2. pl. 3.

So in a Rationabili part bonorum, upon confession of one executor, 28 Hen. 6.
4. pl. 20. 33 Hen. 6. 24. pl. 1.

Ne unques executor found against him shall be general, 11. Hen. 4, 5. 11 Hen.
6. 8. A. Danby.

But the Judgment shall be de bonis testatoris, si, etc. and if not de bonis
propriis, 9 Hen. 7. 15. pl. 1. 2 Edw. 4, 4. 33 Hen. 6. 23. 11 Hen. 6. 10. B.

One pleads ne unques executor, the other plene administraevit, but 40 s. and
found against the former and Judgment given that there should be recovered
against both as much as there was in their Hands and the residue against the
other, 11 Hen. 6. 37. B. Paston. 46 Edw. 3. 9. B.

One dies intestate and Administration is committed to D. by the ordinary and
he comes as servant to D. to administer, absque hoc that he did administer in
any other manner; this is no plea, because he did not show that it was the
ordinary of the place, and Judgment de bonis testatoris, 31 Hen. 6. 13. pl.
(...)
5.

17 Edw. 3. 20. pl. 58. where an executor pleaded non est factum and found
against him, there the Judgment against him for all of the goods of his own as
well as of the goods of the testator, and against the other of the goods that
he had at the day of the writ. vide, 17 Edw. 3. 20. pl. 1. stat. 9. Edw. 3.
cap. 3. statute. 1. 17. Edw. 2. 46. pl. 3.

Plene administravit, the Judgment is for so much of the principal as they had
and for damages de bonis testatoris, si, etc. and if not then for damages de
bonis propriis, and for the residue as much as they had, Coke. 8. part. 134.
Shipleys case. 34. Hen. 6. 32. B. Prisot. com. 440. B. Pepyes case. vide 17
Edw. 3. 66. pl. 83. 46 Edw. 3. 9. pl. 6. Judgment special for the debt.

Upon such plea the defendant prays execution forthwith, because it is a
confession of the debt, but no execution until the defendant had goods of the
testators, Coke. 8. part. Shippleys case. vide 21 Hen. 6. 40.

But if it be found to the defendant no scire facias lies against them, 4 Hen.
6. 4. pl. 8

Unless he prays Judgment upon the plea.

But yet 33 Hen. 6. 24. pl. 1. is that a scire facias lies, yet Coke. 8. part.
53. A. Syms his case, that if it be for land he shall not have a scire facias
because there is no record upon which it may be founded.

Against ^n heir.
If the heir confess the action for as much as did descend, then there shall
be a special Judgment against him of so much as did descend, Com. 440. A.
Pepyes case. 22 Eliz. Dyer. 373. pl. 4. the Judgment Lib. intra. 172. D.

But if he plead any other plea and it be found against him the Judgment shall
be general, Com. 440. Pepyes case.

So if he confess the action and show as much as descends, if it appear to the
court that the profits from the time of the descent until the time of the
execution, are sufficient for the debt, per Dyer. 18. Eliz. Dyer. 344. pl. 1.

1. For the plaintiff. 2. For the defendant. Execution in debt. 3. Of what
Lands. 4. Of what goods.

At the common law it was but a scire facias, Coke. 3. part. 12. or a levari
facias, Coke. 3. part. 12. A. and this is of chattells, and profit of Lands,
and Rents, com. 441. A. Pepyes case.

And this only within the year for if the year were past the party was put to
his action, of debt, Coke. 3. part. 12. A. Harberts case. unless the process be
continued, 33 Hen. 6. 49. pl. 33.

But for Recovery against an heir then it was but one Liberate, com. 441. A.
pepyes case. Lib. intra. 172. D. 173. A. 3 Edw. 3. Execution, 107.

But by Westminster. 2. Cap. 45. a Scire facias was given after the year, and per
Westminster. 2. cap. 18. Elegit was given, Coke 3. part. 12. A.

If a man have an Elegit on Record, and there be a Nichil returned, he shall
have never any other execution, 19 Hen. 6. 4. 5 Edw. 4. 41. 15 Hen. 7. 15.
Fairfax.

And by the 25 Edw. 3. cap. 17. Capias was given in debt: and per consequence a
Capias ad satisfaciendum in Execution. Coke 3. part. 12. A. Harberts case.

Mich. 41 and 42 Eliz. Com. Ban. if the Plaintiff dye after Execution, yet the
Shrieve may levy it, and if there be no Executor or Administrator, the moneys
shall remain in Court. But if the Defendant dye before Execution, there the
Shrieve cannot make Execution; for the words of the Writ are, that it shall be
levied of the goods of the Defendant. Thoroughgoods Case.

Upon a non est inventus returned of the Principal upon Judgment in Com. Ban.
the party shall have Execution against the Bayl, because the debt being by
original is certain, there the Lands which they had at the day of the taking
the recognizance shall be liable, but quaere in ban. Regis if more lands are
liable than they had the day of the original, because the debt is uncertain,
Mich. 15. Jac. ban. Regis. Baskervile et Brocket. special verdict.

The defendant for damages and costs shall have the same execution as the
plaintiff has as if he had recovered against the defendant, per 23 Hen. 8.
cap. 15.

The lands which he had at the time of the Judgment and not before, Coke. 8.
part. 171. Fleetwoods case. 42 Edw. 3. 11. pl. 13. 6. Edw. 193. pl. 14.

But if the Judgment be the last day of the Term the lands which he had the
first day of the term are liable because all the term is but one day in law,
42 Assiz. 17.

If two Joyntenants are for life and he against whom the Judgment is given dies
before execution this shall not be put in execution, 13 Hen. 7. 22. A.

Land in ancient demeasne shall be put in execution, Coke. 5. part. 105. A.
Aldens case. Hill. 11. Jac. com. ban. Rot. 2541. Cox et Barnesly.

The goods that he had at the time of the execution shall be only liable to
execution, Coke. part. 171. A. Fleetwoods case. 2 Hen. 4. 14. 9 Hen. 6. 58. 11
Hen. 4. 7. 34 Hen. 6. 23. B. Prisot. 21 Hen. 7. 87. pl. 1. Crook.

Unless it be in case of executors, 34 Hen. 6. 23. B. Prisot.

But sale by covin after Judgment cannot hinder the execution, 22 Assiz. 72.
13. Hen. 4. 4. pl. 9.

Hill. 40. Eliz. com. Ban. per Curiam, if a writ of execution be awarded for
debt or damages and between the Test of the writ and execution, the party sold
the goods bona fide yet these are liable to the execution.

Ejectment.
In what court it lies.
IT lies not in the Marshalsey, Coke. 10. part. 72. A. Marshalsea.

In Ban. Regis. it lies.

In Com. Ban. it lies.

In the chequer it lies for a party privileged, Coke, 1 part. 3. A. Pelhams
case. and this was by bill.

But if it be by ancient demeasne land it lies not in the court of the King,
Coke. 5. part. 105. A. Aldens case. 9. part. 77. B.

Because the possession is to be removed in such account, per Hobart chief
Justice, Hill. 11. Jac. com. ban. Rot. 25. 41. Cox versus Barnsbee.

But none can plead this but ter-tenant, 2 Hen. 7. 17. pl. 1.

But if the plaintiff do not put in his declaration until the end of the term
the defendant cannot plead ancient demean the next term, but must move the
court that the plaintiff put it in his declaration, and then the advantage
shall be saved. Trin. 12 Jac. ban. Regis.

But he may plead this after veiw because by this he confesses if it be frank
fee or not, 50 Edw. 3. 9. pl. 20.

Who shall have Ejection Firm.
Lessee for years only shall have it, Not. br. Possession
120. F.

And this only upon the possession in deed for he shall not have it upon a
possession in law, 23 Hen. 8. br. quia ejecit, infra, etc. 5.

Nor upon a lease to commence in futuro, 37 Hen. 6. 18. A.

Note that tenant for years needs not count Note.
that he entered, but that a lease was made to him by virtue of which he has
possessed, com. 503 B. Grendons case.

Tenant for years leases to B. at will who is outed by a stranger, tenant for
years shall not have an action because he had not the actual possession,
Pasch. 11. Jac. In the Chequer inter, Sir Rich. Grebham et Stone.

Tenant for years.
Tenant for years leases for one year or a lease is made for years the
remainder for years, estranger enters, none shall have an ejectment but the
tenant in possession, Crook. 130. pl. 99.

Lessee shall have an ejectment after the term ended and recover all in
danages, 21 Lessee.
Edw. 4. 30. pl. 25. Brian. 7. Edw. 4. 6. B. Fairfax.

Lessee which may have a real action cannot have an ejection firm, Com. 419.
B. Bracebridges case.

Husband and wife ought to join if it be in right of the wife, 21 Edw. 4. 10.
pl. 1. 30. pl. Husband and wife.
25. 7 Edw. 4. 6. B. Fairfax. Com. 418. B. Bracebridges case.

But if the term be ended, the husband alone shall have it, because nothing
shall be recovered but damages, 7 Edward. 4. 6. B. Fairfax.

Lessee for one year of a Coppyholder shall have an ejection firm, Coke. ^4.
part. 26. Coppyhold.


Lessee of a Coppyhold for more years shall have an ejection firm although that
such Lease be a forfeiture, for it is a good Lease against all but the Lord,
Trin. 36 Eliz. Ban. Regis Downings case.

Executor^
Executor of a Lessee shall have it, No. Lib. intra. 195. D. Sect. 6.

Executor, Husband and Wife, Co-executor, and the Count. Lib. intra. 252. B.
Sect. 6.

Executor shall have an ejection firm in vit^ Testatoris, per the equity of the
Statute, 4 Ed. 3. cap. 6. Coke 9. part. 78. B. Peytoes case.

Churchwardens.
Churchwardens shall have it of land leased to them, 15 Hen. 7. 8.

Tenant by elegit.
Tennant by Elegit shall not have an ejection firm, Crook 109. pl. 29.

Tenant in common.
Tennant in Common shall have it against his companion, Littleton. 73, A.

Father and Son having several inheritances, the Father levies a fine, the son
being beyondsea dies, his Issue enters and leases (being within age) to A.
without rendering Rent, A. enters, the Conusee enters, and leases it to B. yet
he shall not have an ejectione firmae against A. without express outing,
because as to the moiety the Plaintiff had not title, and the Defendant had
none, because there was no rent reserved, Pasch. 32 Eliz. com. ban. Rott. 1017.
Smye versus June and others.

Against whom Ejectment lies.
Husband and wife.
It lies against Husband and Wife, Lib. intra. 253. C. Sect. 11. Coke 9. part.
77. B. Petoyes case. Com. 187. Wortleyes case.

Estranger
It lies against a stranger that wrongfully outs one, 6 Rich. 2. Ejection.
firm. 2. 21 Edw. 4. 30 pl. 25. Brian. Not. br. 220 F. Coke 9. part. 80. A. 32
Hen. 6. 32. 27. S.

It lies not against a Feoffee of a Lessor, because Feoffee.
he cannot do wrong, Not. br. 198. A. 21 Edw. 4. 10. pl. 1. Choke. 21 Edw. 4.
30. 32 Hen. 6. 32. pl. 27. 38 Edw. 3. 33. pl. 44.

Unless the Feoffee make a Deed presently upon the outing, then it lies against
him, Not. br. 198. A.

Or enter upon the Lessee, afterward that the Lessee had entered upon him, Not.
br. 198. A.

Lessor grants a Reversion to A. the Lessee Grantor.
attornes, A. outs him, the Lessee shall have an ejectione firmae, Not. br. 221.
A. 1 Hen. 5. 3. pl. 3.

Heir.
It lies against the Heir of the Lessor, Not. br. 198. K.

Lessor.
It lies against the Lessor (...) outs the Lessee, Not. br. 220. F. 21 Edw. 4.
10. pl. 1. Choke. 30. pl. 25. 38 Edw. 3. 33. pl. 44. Coke. 9. part. 80. A. Not.
br. 198. K.

Recoveror
Lessor suffers a Recovery, the Recoveror outs the Lessee, he shall have an
Ejectione Firmae against the Recoveror by the equity of the Statute, 21 Hen. 8.
cap. 15. Not. br. 220. J. 198. E.

Lord.
It lies against the Lord per Escheate which outs one, Not. br. 221. I. B. 198.
K.

It lies against the Lord of a Villeyn which enters upon the Termor, Not. br.
221. C. 198. K.

Tenant in common.
It lies against Tenant in common per his companion, Littleton. 73. A.

Of what things an Ejectment lies.
Cattle.
It lies upon a lease for Cattle because it is a personal thing, 1 Hen. 6. 1
Cottesmore.

Wood.
It lies of Wood, Com. 223. B. Barkeleyes case, the count there. Chamber.


It lies of a chamber, Mich. 30. Eliz. ban. Regis. Brand against Cage.

Tithes.
It lies of Tithes, per 32 Hen. 8. cap. 7. 2. 3. Mariae. Dyer. 116. pl. 17. the
count ought to show the nature or quality of the Tithes, Coke. 11. part. 24. B.
Harpers case.

Garden, etc.
It lies of a Garden, Barn, and Tyths, 9 Eliz. Dyer. 258. pl. 16.

But if all the Tything consists of a modus decimandi and a lease made thereof
ejectione firm lies not, Coke 11. part. 25. B. Harpers Case.

Watercourse.
It lies of a watercourse, Com. 288. B. Brown. Regist. orig. 227. B.

Hundred.
It lies of a Hundred, because it is liberum tenementum, 15 Hen. 7. 8. Pl. 1.

Manor.
It lies of a Manor, and the Writ Regist. orig. 227. B. Not. br. 220. G. Com.
229. A. Barkleys Case.

The Count. Lib. intr. 252. A. Sect. 4.

Count of a demise of 300 Acres by the name of a Manor: habendum Manerium cum,

Message.
It lies of a Message, Coke 11. part. 55. A. Savels Case.

The Count, No. Lib. intra. 184. A. Sect. 1. 3. 197. C. Sect. 7. Lib. intra.

It lies de tribus partibus duorum Messuagiorum, No. Lib. intra. 195. D. Sect.

Chapel.
It is not formal to have it of a Chapel, but shall be of a House, Coke 11.

Mill.
It lies of a Mill, No. Lib. Intra. 192. A. Sect. 5.

Pasture.
It lies of 300 Acres of Pasture, the Count Lib. intra. 251. D. Sect. 2.

Ox.
It lies of pasturing of an Ox, Com. 228. B. Brown. Regist. 227. B.

Meadow.
It lies of 100 Acres of Meadow, Lib. intra. 252. A. Sect. 13.

Rectory.
It lies of a Rectory, 15 Hen. 8. pl. 1. 16 Hen. 7. 8. pl. 6. 13 and 14 Eliz.
Dyer. 304. pl. 25. The Count Lib. intra. 253. A. Sect. 9, 10.

Reversion
It lies not of a Reversion, Com. 159. B. Thracies Case per Dyer.

Land.
It lies of a 100 acres of Land: the Count Lib. intra. 251. C. Sect. 1.

But it lies not of a Close containing three acres, but shall be of so many of
the acres by name, Coke 11. part. 55. Savels Case.

For by Crook Justice, Mich. 15 Jac. Wicks and Sparrow, the Land of every man
is enclosed, and therefore an Ejectione firmae cannot lie of it for the
incertainty.

But Coke 11. part. 55. Savels Case was, it seems, that if it be of a Close
containing three acres of pasture, it is good because the quantity is showed,
and so it was adjudged, Mich. 15 Jac. ban. Regis. Wicks et Sparrow.

It lies not of a piece of ground called Michels piece, Trin. 38 Eliz. ban.
Regis. Rott. 450. Palmer and Humphreys.

It lies not of a virge of Land, 38 Eliz. Rott. 453. Mell versus Moor.

The Count Generally.
Bishop.
If it be of a Lease made by a Bishop, it ought to count upon the Deed, No Lib.
intra. 186. D. sect. 2.

Husband and wife.
But if it be of a Lease made by the Husband and Wife, it needs not count that
it was by Indenture, Lib. intra. 252. C. sect. 8. Coke 2. part. 61. B. Wiscots
case.

Person.
If it be of a Lease made by a Person tunc and adhuc seized of the Reversion,
it is good without averring of the life of the Person, 13 and 14 Eliz. Dyer
304. pl. 52.

If the count be of a Lease made by three where two have nothing in it, it is
not good, although they join in the Lease, but contrary by him that has right,
per Williams and Crook. Mich. 10 Jac. Ban. Regis. Longs case.

Lease.
A Lease to commence at Mich. next after the death of A. the count ought to
show that A. is dead, 1 Mariae. Dyer 97. pl. 46. and fol. 89^ 19 Eliz. Dyer
357. pl. 46.

Demise.
Counts that A. demised to him per Indenture dated 27 Martii, 11 Jac. and
primum delibat. 10 de^imo Aprilis eodem anno, for 21 year till Mich. next
before, and the ejectment 1^ Aprilis, this is good; or he may count, that by
Indenture dated 27 Martii, and primum de^ libat. 10 Aprilis, Mich. 11. Jac.
ban. Regis. Michels case.

The count upon the Imparlance Roll wa^ upon a Lease made 10. of December, 10
Ja^ and upon the plea-roll it was upon a Lease made 30 Januarii, 10 Jac.
habendum 20 of December before, this is not good, Hill. 14 Jac. Milward and
Wats. Ban. Regis.

The count was that he was seized, and so seized, leased, 9 Eliz. Dyer 258. pl.
16. Com. 416. A. Bracebridges case. Com. 187. A. Adams case, Com. 223. B.
Barkleys case Com. 530. B. Howel and Crofts case.

But 14. Eliz. Dyer. 340. pl 57. does not count of the seism, Coke 11. part.
3. B. Coke 3. part. 16. A. Borastons case. Coke 3. part. 45. Browns case. Coke
4. part. 96. A. Lamberts case. Com. 459. B. Studs case. Com. 504. B. Snowes
case.

The Writ.
In Wales it may be by plaint without an original Writ, for this action is out
of the Statute, 26 Hen. 8. cap. 6. Hill. 36. Eliz. ban. Regis 610. Griffin
versus Eliot and Wilkins.

It is Vi and armis, 1 Hen. 5. 3. Coke 9. part. 78. A. Petoes case. 21 Edw. 10.
pl. 1. Choke.

But Hill. 36 Eliz. ban. Regis Rott. 610. Griffin versus Eliot and Wilkins in
error, that it may be without vi et armis, 7 Hen. 6. 4. 17 Edw. 3. 1.

Fuit ad terminum qui nondum praeteriit, 2 et 3 Mariae. Dyer 116. pl. 71.

Et est pone per vad. et salvos pleg. 21 Edw. 4. 10. pl. 1. et 31 pl. 25. Brian.

It may be bona et catalla, Com. 228. B. Lib. intra. 252. B. Sect. 7, 8.

Although Regist. orig. 227. B. say to the contrary.

But may be without it, Com. 229. A. 199. A. Adams Case.

The Process 1. before, 2. after appearance.
The Process is Attach and distress and Process of Outlary, Not. br. 220. H. 35
Hen. 6. 6. per Wangford and Moyl. Com. 228. B. Coke 9. part. 78. A. Peytoes
Case.

The Bar.
Accord.
Accord with satisfaction a good bar, Coke 9. part. 78. A Petoyes Case,
because it is but in the nature of a Trespass.

Dures.
Dures a good bar, Lib. intra. 253. B. Sect. 10.

Ejecit.
Non ejecit a good bar, si bona and catalla are not in the Writ, 7 Edw. 6. 89.
pl. 111. 19 Hen. 6. 56.

But if such words be in, Quaere.

Ent^ie.
The Lessor had it but in right of his wife, and he enters after the death of
the Lessor in right of his wife, Lib. intra. 252. D. Sect. 8.

Surrender
That he surrend^ed before, and quod non ejecit a good bar, 21 Edw. 4. 10. pl.
1. 30 pl. 25.

The Judgment.
The judgment shall be quod recuperet against the Defendant terminum suum
praedictum venturum de and in, etc. ac dampna sua, etc. and quod Defend.
capiatur. 9. Eliz. Dyer 258. pl. 16. 7 Edw. 6. Dyer 89. pl. 109. Com. 420. A.
Bracebridges case. 515. Snowes case. Lib. intra. 253, A. Sect. 8. 256. C. Sect.
13. 259. C. Sect. 15. No. Lib. intra. 188. A. pl. 7. 203. A. Sect. 8. 212. D.
Sect. 11. 216. B. Sect. 13. Com. 526. A. Granthams case.

Note.
But note this is, when the term is not ended, Coke 9. part. 80. A. Peytoes
case. 4. part. 104. Lamberts case. Not. br. 220. H. 7 Edw. 4. 6. 13. Hen. 7.
20. B. Wood.

Note also, he shall recover damages but for the ejectment, Coke* 9. part. 80.
A. Peytoes case.

If the Term be ended he shall recover all in damages, 7 Edw. 4. 6. Fairfax.
No. Lib. intra. 205. D. Sect. 9.

Judgment. First for the Plaintiff, Com. 526. Granthams case. Secondly for the
Defendant, No. Lib. intra. 197. C. Sect. 6.

Judgment upon a Nonsuit after Evidence delivered to the Jury. No. Lib.
intra. 189. B. Sect. 2.

Quare Impedit Ne admittas. Quare non admisit. Quare incumbravit.

Quid.
IMpedire est pedem ponere in jus alienum, quod quis habet in jure
praesentandi, Bracton. lib. 4. cap. 6. fol. 247. A.

Haec dictio [impedit] componitur de [in] and [pes] and unde revera ille
impedit, qui nititur intus pedem ponere in jus alienum, ubi nullum jus ei
competit, nec proprietatis, nec possessionis, Bracton lib. ibidem.

Advowson is an interest to present an able man to a benefice, 5 Hen. 7. 38. B.
Brian and Townsend.

Advocation est incorporalis, and est jus praesentandi ad ecclesiam vacantem,
Bracton lib. 2. fol. 53. A.

Jus patronatus est Honorificum, to be Patron or Protector. Vtile, to advance
his friend. Onerosum, a burden to his conscience if he present one not able.

In what Court it lies.
Bracton Lib. 3. fol. 160. A. Immediate in curia Domini Regis terminarid ebent
placita de advocation ^t us Ecclesiarum, quia si alius a Rege mandaret
^piscopis de admittendo Clericum, and ipse oltem^ rabit alius a Rege coercionem
non haberet, quia Episcopus ad alterius mandatum quam Regis Clericum admittere
non tenetur.

Quare Impedit of an Advowson in Wales ought to be in com. ban. in England, and
shall be tried in the County next adjoining to Wales; and the reason is,
because the Lords there have not power to send to the Bishop, 36 Hen. 6. 33. B.
Fortescue. 35 Hen. 6. 30. pl. 35. 3 Edw. 3. 163. pl. 35. 8 Edw. 3. 319. pl. 15.
24 Edw. 3. 3. pl. 26.

No plea to the Jurisdiction, to say, that it is ancient demean, because they
cannot award a Writ to the Bishop, 7 Hen 6. 35.

In Ban. Regis it lies for the King, for he may sue there if he pleases, Not.
br. 3^. G. 47 Edw. 3. 4. pl. 9.

The King grants Majori Ballivis and juratis quinque portuum, that they shall
not be impleaded for no Land in no Court, nor for other cause, unless it be
within the Five Ports, scil. at Shepway, before the Warden of the five Ports:
this extends not to a Quare Impedit, 21 Hen. 7. 88. pl. 7. Crook.

Who shall have a Quare Impedit.
Note.
That he that is out of the possession shall not have a Quare Impedit, which a
man may be five ways, 1. by Presentation, 2. by discontinuance of the Land, to
which, etc. 3. by Disseisin. 4. by Descent. 5. by Recovery. in right of the
Advowson, or Quare Impedit.

Husband and Wife having it in jure uxoris, they join in a Quare impedit, Coke
5. part. 57. Specots case. 50 Edw. 3. 13. pl. 4. 7 Hen. 7. 2. B. 38 Hen. 6. 3.
pl. 9. 28 Hen. 6. 8. pl. 3.

But the Husband may bring this without the Wife, 14 Hen. 4. 12. pl. 12. 22
Rich. 2. br. 937. for the wrong done to the Husband.

The church void, the Wife dies, the Husband shall have the Quare Impedit,
because the presentation was a Chattel invested, 21 Hen. 6. 56.

The Husband presents, and after they are divorced, the Husband shall have the
Writ, 31 Hen. 8. br. Divorce 8.

Cestui que use.
Cestui que use shall not have it, but the Feoffees; for the presentation, is
always firm to the Advowson, Crook 17. Hen. 7. A. Frowick and ibidem 2 Hen.
8. 160. B. pl. 1.

Chancellor.
Chancellor shall present to a church under 20 Marks per annum, which are
belonging to the Crown, but not if the King have them by other Title, Not. br.
35. K. 38 Edw. 3. 3. pl. 14. Com. 528. B.

But vide Br. Praescript. 86. that at this day the Chancellor presents to all
under 20 l. per Annum.

Defendant.
The Defendant shall have a Quare Impedit against the Plaintiff, if his Clerk be
not instituted, Not. br. 35. C.

Half blood.
The elder brother presents and dies, the brother by the half blood shall not
have the next avoydance. Not. br. 36. E. 3 Hen. 7. 5.

But the 19 Edw. 2. Quare impedit 177. Contra.

Two Sisters by several venters make composition, and one dies before
Presentment, the other shall have it, Not. br. 36. E. Corporation.


The Bishop shall have a Quare Impedit ratione Patronatus. Bishop.


Ratione patronatus
Patronage of a Denary belongs to him of common right, 17 Edw. 3. 40. pl. 17.

Ratione Lapsus.
The Bishop shall have a Quare impedit ratione lapsus, and the Writ shall be
general, but the Count shall be of the Collation, Not. br. 33 D. 17 Edw. 3. 64.
pl. 69. Lib. intra. 501. A.

If Lapse accrue to the Metropolitan, he may put his Clerk in without the
Ordinary of the place. Doct. and Stud. 125. B.

The Ordinary is deprived after Lapse accrues, Quere who shall have it, 7 Edw.
6. Dyer 87. pl. 203.

In quo casu Ordinarius loci providebit ecclesiae viduitati, Bracton. Lib. 2.
34. fol. 76. B.

But Bracton says, Lib. 3. that Lapse was but by the Council of Lateran.

If it be found for one Patron in a jure Patronatus, and the Presenter prays
not to be admitted, the Ordinary shall present by Lapse, 34 Hen. 6. 12. pl. 22.

Although a Ne admittas be sued, yet the Ordinary of the place shall present by
Lapse Not. br. 48. L

Lapse is when the Patron does not present in six Months, then the Ordinary
presents by Lapse, Doct. and Stud. 124. B.

Although the Patron be an Infant or feme covert, Not. br. 34. T. 3 Edw. 3.
Quare Impedit. 41.

But this rule of Lapse admits diverse exceptions, ^cill.

1 So long as the Church is void the Patron may present Doct. et Student. 126.
A. for the Title by Lapse is not a Chattell invested.

2. It shall not be Lapse of a chapel Donative or Chantry unless the patron
make his presentative, then it shall, Not. br. 35. E. 6 Hen. 7. br. presentment
43. Pasch. 3. Jac. Ban. Regis. Fairfeild versus Gaire, or expressed in the
foundation, 13 Edw. 4. 3.

3. An Advowson appropriate shall not be Lapsed, Not. br. 35. F.

4. If the ordinary be named a disturber in the Quare Impedit, 5 Edw. 3. 2. B.
22 Hen. 6. 28. And at this day he is named in the writ to prevent the lapse, 39
Edw. 3 15. pl. 4. Statham.

For otherways the Lapse incurres, 5 Edw. 4. 115. but it seems that the
ordinary cannot collate him that was the incumbent and made defendant in the
suite.

5. In many cases Lapse shall not incur without notice.

In what case Lapse cannot incur without notice.
1. Upon a Resignation, Not. br. 35. H. 1 Hen. 7. 9. 5 Edw. 4. 116. A.

If the Ordinary dies his Successor ought to give notice, Crook. 18 Hen. 7.
41. pl. 2.

2. Upon privation, Not. br. 35. H. 1 Hen. 7. 9. 5 Edw. 4. 118. A.

Although the Incumbent be merely Laicus, 13 Eliz. Dyer. 293. pl. 3.

And although the party be party to the Suit, Coke 6. part. 29. Greens case, 22
Eliz. Dyer 369. pl. 54.

Although the Title of Lapse be devolved to the King, per lapsum temporis, 18
Eliz. Dyer 348. pl. 12. 22 Eliz. Dyer 369. pl. 54.

3. If it be litigious, 34 Hen. 6. 40. B. Prisot. Lib. intra. 511. D.

4. If the Church be void by any clause of Statute, 13 Eliz. cap. 12.

5. He shall lose his benefice, per 2 Edw. 6. cap. 20. for refusing to pay
tithes, 12 Eliz. Dyer 294. pl. 3.

6. If one have a benefice within 8 l. per ann. takes another and be inducted,
Coke 4. part. 79.

7. If the former be 8 l. without induction, no lapse without notice, Coke 4.
part. 79. B. Digbies case.

But after induction no notice is requisite, Coke 4. part. 75. 7 Eliz. Dyer
237. pl. 29. 8 Eliz. Dyer 255. pl. 5.

And the value shall be according to the true value, and not according to the
book of Tithes and first fruits, 7 Eliz. Dyer 237. pl. 29.

8. Upon refusal of a Clerk, Not. br. 35. J. 15 Eliz. Dyer 327. pl. 7.

But Crook 18 Hen. 7. 49. pl. 2. per Frowick, if it be a spiritual Patron,
then it is not requisite.

So for avoydance per Creation, Cession, or Death, Doct. and Stud. 116. B. 5
Edw. 4. 115.

After privation the Patron grants the Advowson to A. the Ordinary collates A.
he cannot be removed, for notice ought not to be given him, for it was void to
all but the Grantor, Mich. 42 and 43 Eliz. com. ban. Rot. 3579. Leake against
the Bishop of Coventrie.

Notice is as to the Lapse only, for as to the presentation, the Patron may be
put out of the possession of the presentation although no notice is given,
Pasc. 39 Eliz. com. ban. Scriven versus Episcopum Lincoln.

Parson.
A Parson shall have a Quare impedit for the Vicaridge, for of common right it
belongs unto him, Not. br. 33. V.

For if the Vicaridge be void, and the Parson be made a Bishop, yet he shall
present, for it was a Chattel invested, Not. br. 34. N. 24 Edw. 3. 26.

A Parson imprisoned shall have a Quare Impedit, 17 Edw. 3. 51. pl. 25.

Prebendary.
Prebendary, although he resign after usurpation upon him, 26 Edw. 3. 3.

Dean and Chapter.
The Chapter brought a Quare impedit against the Dean, and good, for their
possessions are several, 9 Edw. 3. 134. and fol. 354. pl. 33. 17 Edw. 3. 64. 40
Edw. 3. 28. B. Finchden. 7 Edw. 3. Quare impedit 72. Lib. intra. 500. A.

Aggregate
Hospital which has not spiritual possessions, neither College nor scal, yet
the Master shall have a Quare Impedit.

Corporation mixed.
1. In right of the Crown, Not. br. 32. E. the Writ.

2. For by reason of Lapse, for this makes him supreme Patron, Doct. and
Student. 124. B. Com. 498. 18 Edw. 3. 19.

Therefore, after Lapse accrues to the King, the Patron cannot present, Doct.
and Stud. 126. A. 10 Eliz. Dyer 277. pl. 55.

Nor the Ordinary collate after Lapse is accrewed to the King, 17 Eliz. Dyer
339. pl. 47.

In his own right.
But in case where notice is requisite, the King cannot present without notice,
18 Eliz. Dyer 348. pl. 12. 22 Eliz. Dyer 369. pl. 54.

If the Dean of the Chapel Royal presents not within 6 months, the King shall
present, Not. br. 34. F. 27 Edw. 3. 84.

Creation.
Parson created Bishop, the King shall present 21 Edw. 3. 31. pl. 14. and fol.
41. 11 Hen. 4. 37. vide 6. Eliz. Dyer. 228.

Ratione temperalium.
21 Edw. 3. 5. pl. 13. The Writ was quia pertinet ad Regem praesentare ratione
Episcopatus nuper vacantis, and good.

The Count Lib. intra. 530. C. sect. 15.

And needs not say in the Count, for that the temporalities were seized, 42
Edw. 3. 7. pl. 27.

If a Church be void, during the time that the temporalities are in the hands
of the King, although he makes restitution, yet the King shall present, Not.
br. 33. N. Stanford 44. Edw. 3. 17. pl. 8. 18 Edw. 3. 22. pl. 39.

If the Church voids, and the Bishop dies, the King shall have it, and not the
Executors, Not. br. 33. Q. 9 Edw. 3. 2. Quare imped. 11.

And although the Bishop collate, Not. br. 34. K. 11 Hen. 4. 9. A. 24 Edw. 3.
30. 44 Edw. 3. 3.

But if he dye after induction, although it be the same day, the King shall not
have it, 44 Edw. 3. 3.

Lapse accrues to the Bishop which dies, the King presents, 25 Edw. 3. 53. pl.
20.

Lapse accrues after the death of the Bishop, the King presents, Not. br. 34. G.

Outlary.
So if he have judgment to have the temporalities, 21 Edw. 3. 29.

By Outlary in a personal action the King shall present, Not. br. 34. R. 8
Rich. 2. Quare Impedit 200. 21 Hen. 6. 56.

A. enfeoffes B. of a Manor, to which, etc. and is outlawed, and presents per
permission Symony.
of B. the King shall present, because the presentation is a chattel, 5 Hen. 5.
pl. 4.

Upon 31 Eliz. cap. 6.

Note.
The pleadings, No. Lib. intra. 405. C. Sect. 516. B. 531. D.

Note per 25 Edw. 3. cap. 1. the King shall not present in another right, but
for the avoydance in his own time, 11 Hen. 4. 7. pl. 16.

Note, if the King presents one that dies before induction the King shall
present again, for he had it not complete before, Coke 9. part. Holts case.
Vide Regist. orig. 31. B.

But if the King have title hac vice, and another presents A. which dies, the
King has lost his turn, Coke 7. part. 28. Baskerviles case. No. lib. intra.
489. A.

Yet if one be qualified having two benefices takes another incompatible, the
first is void, by two years the Patron presents, and after induction, his Clerk
refuses to pay his tenths, and this is certified according to the Statute of 26
Hen. 8. the Bishop being Patron collates, the King shall present for this
refusal is as it were a resignation, which shall be intended a Collusion, to
take away the title of the King, Mich. 29 and 30 Eliz. Com. Ban. Bott. 2299.
the King against the Bishop of Lincoln.

12 Eliz. Dyer 292. pl. 70. 25 Edw. 47. the King presents to a Prebendary
ratione temporalium, and revokes it before instalment, and yet he is inducted,
the King confirms it, and he is made Bishop, the Prebend dies, the King shall
present again, for the confirmation was void, because he was not in ex
praesentatione Regis.

Not. br. 38. D. the King recovers a Prebendary, and gives by Letters Pattents
to A. which dies, the King gives it to B. he shall have a Writ to the Justices
to make execution for him.

Disseisee.
Disseisee shall have a Quare Impedit before his entry into the Manor, to
which the Advowson belongs, 21 Hen. 6. 9. B. 19 Hen. 6. 33. 33 Hen. 6. 33. B.
Not. br. 33. Q. 24 Hen. 8. Dyer 5. pl. 6. Crook. 6 Hen. 8. 169. A. Pollard.

Disseisor presents, Disseisee enters into the Manor to which, etc. and
presents, he shall have a Quare Impedit, if it be within six months, 14 Hen. 6.
24. Fulthorp.

And if the Disseisor presents, and the disseiseisee enters into the Manor, to
which, etc. and infeoffes B. thereof, with the Advowson, the Church voyds, B.
shall have a Quare Impedit, for by the entry of the Disseisee, he was in the
possession of the Advowson, 3 Hen. 4. 7. pl. 33. 14 Hen. 6. 16. pl. 52.

But 33 Hen. 6. 33. Prisot to the contrary, for there it is said, that until
Recovery the Disseisee shall not have the Advowson.

Disseisor dies seized of a Manor to which the Advowson belongs, the Disseisee
shall not have a Quare Impedit, 24 Hen. 8. Dyer 5. pl. 6. 33 Hen. 6. 33 B. vide
19 Hen. 6. 33.

But if it void in the time of the Disseisor, the Disseisee shall have it,
although the Disseisor died seized of the Manor to which, etc. 24 Hen. 8. Dyer
5. pl. 6.

Disseisor suffers usurpation, Disseisee enters into the Manor, Disseisee
shall have a Quare Impedit, Not. br. 36. F. 14 Hen. 6. 14. 3 Hen. 4. 7.

Executor.
Executor of the King shall not have a Quare Impedit, but the successor, for
this is a chattel Royal, 7 Hen. 4. 25. pl. 3. 1 Edw. 3. 17. pl. 8. 5 Edw. 3.
149. pl. 15.

Executor of a common person shall have a presentment to a Church, which was
void in the time of the Testator, although the Testator were but Tenant in
Tail, Not. br. 33. P. and V.

Although the Heir be in ward to the King, Not. br. 33. R.

If one recover in a Quare Impedit and dye* the Heir shall not have execution
against the Executors, 9 Hen. 6. 57. A. Rolfe.

Enfant.
At the Common Law the Infant was bound by suffering Usurpation, 35. Hen. 6. 6.
31 Edw. 3. Quare Impedit. 186. 10 Edw. 2. Quare Impedit. 43.

But at this day he is not, per Westminster. 2. cap. 5.

Unless he be a Purchaser, 10 Edw. 2. Quare Impedit. 43. 35 Hen. 6. 60. Not.
br. 31. and 34.

Or that the party that usurps be remitted, Not. br. 35. M.
